- <span class="s1" style="font-variant-numeric: normal; font-variant-east-asian: normal; font-variant-alternates: normal; font-kerning: auto; font-optical-sizing: auto; font-feature-settings: normal; font-variation-settings: normal; font-variant-position: normal; font-stretch: normal; font-size: 12px; line-height: normal;"></span>debugfs: Manually view and modify the filesystem structure, such as undeleting a file or extracting a corrupted file
- <span class="s1" style="font-variant-numeric: normal; font-variant-east-asian: normal; font-variant-alternates: normal; font-kerning: auto; font-optical-sizing: auto; font-feature-settings: normal; font-variation-settings: normal; font-variant-position: normal; font-stretch: normal; font-size: 12px; line-height: normal;"></span>dumpe2fs: Display block and superblock group information
- <span class="s1" style="font-variant-numeric: normal; font-variant-east-asian: normal; font-variant-alternates: normal; font-kerning: auto; font-optical-sizing: auto; font-feature-settings: normal; font-variation-settings: normal; font-variant-position: normal; font-stretch: normal; font-size: 12px; line-height: normal;"></span>e2label: Change the label on the filesystem
- <span class="s1" style="font-variant-numeric: normal; font-variant-east-asian: normal; font-variant-alternates: normal; font-kerning: auto; font-optical-sizing: auto; font-feature-settings: normal; font-variation-settings: normal; font-variant-position: normal; font-stretch: normal; font-size: 12px; line-height: normal;"></span>resize2fs: Expand or shrink a filesystem
- <span class="s1" style="font-variant-numeric: normal; font-variant-east-asian: normal; font-variant-alternates: normal; font-kerning: auto; font-optical-sizing: auto; font-feature-settings: normal; font-variation-settings: normal; font-variant-position: normal; font-stretch: normal; font-size: 12px; line-height: normal;"></span>tune2fs: Modify filesystem parameters

- <span class="s1" style="font-variant-numeric: normal; font-variant-east-asian: normal; font-variant-alternates: normal; font-kerning: auto; font-optical-sizing: auto; font-feature-settings: normal; font-variation-settings: normal; font-variant-position: normal; font-stretch: normal; font-size: 12px; line-height: normal;"></span>XFS Filesystem Tools

- <span class="s1" style="font-variant-numeric: normal; font-variant-east-asian: normal; font-variant-alternates: normal; font-kerning: auto; font-optical-sizing: auto; font-feature-settings: normal; font-variation-settings: normal; font-variant-position: normal; font-stretch: normal; font-size: 12px; line-height: normal;"></span>xfs_admin: Display or change filesystem parameters such as the label or UUID assigned
- <span class="s1" style="font-variant-numeric: normal; font-variant-east-asian: normal; font-variant-alternates: normal; font-kerning: auto; font-optical-sizing: auto; font-feature-settings: normal; font-variation-settings: normal; font-variant-position: normal; font-stretch: normal; font-size: 12px; line-height: normal;"></span>xfs_db: Examine and debug an XFS filesystem
- <span class="s1" style="font-variant-numeric: normal; font-variant-east-asian: normal; font-variant-alternates: normal; font-kerning: auto; font-optical-sizing: auto; font-feature-settings: normal; font-variation-settings: normal; font-variant-position: normal; font-stretch: normal; font-size: 12px; line-height: normal;"></span>xfs_fsr: Improve the organization of mounted filesystems
- <span class="s1" style="font-variant-numeric: normal; font-variant-east-asian: normal; font-variant-alternates: normal; font-kerning: auto; font-optical-sizing: auto; font-feature-settings: normal; font-variation-settings: normal; font-variant-position: normal; font-stretch: normal; font-size: 12px; line-height: normal;"></span>xfs_info: Display information about a mounted filesystem, including the block sizes and sector sizes, as well as label and UUID information
- <span class="s1" style="font-variant-numeric: normal; font-variant-east-asian: normal; font-variant-alternates: normal; font-kerning: auto; font-optical-sizing: auto; font-feature-settings: normal; font-variation-settings: normal; font-variant-position: normal; font-stretch: normal; font-size: 12px; line-height: normal;"></span>xfs_repair: Repair corrupted or damaged XFS filesystems

- <span class="s1" style="font-variant-numeric: normal; font-variant-east-asian: normal; font-variant-alternates: normal; font-kerning: auto; font-optical-sizing: auto; font-feature-settings: normal; font-variation-settings: normal; font-variant-position: normal; font-stretch: normal; font-size: 12px; line-height: normal;"></span>$ fsck —> check and repair a Linux filesystem. a front end to several different programs that check the various filesystems.

- <span class="s1" style="font-variant-numeric: normal; font-variant-east-asian: normal; font-variant-alternates: normal; font-kerning: auto; font-optical-sizing: auto; font-feature-settings: normal; font-variation-settings: normal; font-variant-position: normal; font-stretch: normal; font-size: 12px; line-height: normal;"></span>If any discrepancies occur, run the fsck program in repair mode, and it will attempt to reconcile the discrepancies and fix the filesystem. If the fsck program is unable to repair the drive on the first run, try running it again a few times to fix any broken files and directory links.
- <span class="s1" style="font-variant-numeric: normal; font-variant-east-asian: normal; font-variant-alternates: normal; font-kerning: auto; font-optical-sizing: auto; font-feature-settings: normal; font-variation-settings: normal; font-variant-position: normal; font-stretch: normal; font-size: 12px; line-height: normal;"></span>$ sudo fsck -f /dev/sdb1

———————————————

**GUI:**

- <span class="s1" style="font-variant-numeric: normal; font-variant-east-asian: normal; font-variant-alternates: normal; font-kerning: auto; font-optical-sizing: auto; font-feature-settings: normal; font-variation-settings: normal; font-variant-position: normal; font-stretch: normal; font-size: 12px; line-height: normal;"></span>A windows manager is a program that communicates with the display server (sometimes called a windows server) on behalf of the UI.
- <span class="s1" style="font-variant-numeric: normal; font-variant-east-asian: normal; font-variant-alternates: normal; font-kerning: auto; font-optical-sizing: auto; font-feature-settings: normal; font-variation-settings: normal; font-variant-position: normal; font-stretch: normal; font-size: 12px; line-height: normal;"></span>Each particular desktop environment has its own default window manager, such as Mutter, Kwin, Muffin, Marco, and Metacity.
- <span class="s1" style="font-variant-numeric: normal; font-variant-east-asian: normal; font-variant-alternates: normal; font-kerning: auto; font-optical-sizing: auto; font-feature-settings: normal; font-variation-settings: normal; font-variant-position: normal; font-stretch: normal; font-size: 12px; line-height: normal;"></span>The display server is a program that uses a communication protocol to transmit the desires of the UI to the operating system, and vice versa. The communication protocol, called the display server protocol, can operate over a network. A compositor program arranges various display elements within a window to create a screen image to be passed back to the client.
- <span class="s1" style="font-variant-numeric: normal; font-variant-east-asian: normal; font-variant-alternates: normal; font-kerning: auto; font-optical-sizing: auto; font-feature-settings: normal; font-variation-settings: normal; font-variant-position: normal; font-stretch: normal; font-size: 12px; line-height: normal;"></span>The X Window System (X for short) is the display server used for Linux systems. It was developed in the 1980s. in Linux there was only one software package that supported X, called XFree86.<span class="Apple-converted-space"> </span> in 2004 the XFree86 project changed their licensing requirements, which caused many Linux distributions to switch to the X.Org foundation’s implementation of X, simply called X.Org. many distributions created their own customizations of the X.Org server; thus, you will see a wide variety of names concerning the Linux X display server, such as X.org-X11, X, X11, and X.Org Server.
- <span class="s1" style="font-variant-numeric: normal; font-variant-east-asian: normal; font-variant-alternates: normal; font-kerning: auto; font-optical-sizing: auto; font-feature-settings: normal; font-variation-settings: normal; font-variant-position: normal; font-stretch: normal; font-size: 12px; line-height: normal;"></span>Within the past few years, a new X display server package called Wayland has made headway in the Linux world.

X.org

- <span class="s1" style="font-variant-numeric: normal; font-variant-east-asian: normal; font-variant-alternates: normal; font-kerning: auto; font-optical-sizing: auto; font-feature-settings: normal; font-variation-settings: normal; font-variant-position: normal; font-stretch: normal; font-size: 12px; line-height: normal;"></span>The X.Org package keeps track of display card, monitor, and input device information in a configuration file, using the original XFree86 format. The primary configuration file is /etc/X11/xorg.conf, though the file is sometimes stored in the /etc/ directory. Typically, however, this file is no longer used.
- <span class="s1" style="font-variant-numeric: normal; font-variant-east-asian: normal; font-variant-alternates: normal; font-kerning: auto; font-optical-sizing: auto; font-feature-settings: normal; font-variation-settings: normal; font-variant-position: normal; font-stretch: normal; font-size: 12px; line-height: normal;"></span>Individual applications or devices store their own X11 settings in separate files stored in the /etc/X11/xorg.conf.d directory.
- <span class="s1" style="font-variant-numeric: normal; font-variant-east-asian: normal; font-variant-alternates: normal; font-kerning: auto; font-optical-sizing: auto; font-feature-settings: normal; font-variation-settings: normal; font-variant-position: normal; font-stretch: normal; font-size: 12px; line-height: normal;"></span>The X.Org software can detect most common hardware devices, so no manual configuration is required. in some cases, auto-detection might not work properly, and you need to make X11 configuration changes. In this case, you can manually create the configuration file. To do this, shut down the X Server by going to a command prompt, using the command sudo telinit 3, and using super user privileges to generate the file via the Xorg -configure command. The file, named xorg.conf.new, will be in your local directory. Make any necessary tweaks, rename the file, move the file to its proper location, and restart the X server
- <span class="s1" style="font-variant-numeric: normal; font-variant-east-asian: normal; font-variant-alternates: normal; font-kerning: auto; font-optical-sizing: auto; font-feature-settings: normal; font-variation-settings: normal; font-variant-position: normal; font-stretch: normal; font-size: 12px; line-height: normal;"></span>xorg.conf Sections Information:

- <span class="s1" style="font-variant-numeric: normal; font-variant-east-asian: normal; font-variant-alternates: normal; font-kerning: auto; font-optical-sizing: auto; font-feature-settings: normal; font-variation-settings: normal; font-variant-position: normal; font-stretch: normal; font-size: 12px; line-height: normal;"></span>Input Device: Configures the session’s keyboard and mouse
- <span class="s1" style="font-variant-numeric: normal; font-variant-east-asian: normal; font-variant-alternates: normal; font-kerning: auto; font-optical-sizing: auto; font-feature-settings: normal; font-variation-settings: normal; font-variant-position: normal; font-stretch: normal; font-size: 12px; line-height: normal;"></span>Monitor: Sets the session’s monitor configuration
- <span class="s1" style="font-variant-numeric: normal; font-variant-east-asian: normal; font-variant-alternates: normal; font-kerning: auto; font-optical-sizing: auto; font-feature-settings: normal; font-variation-settings: normal; font-variant-position: normal; font-stretch: normal; font-size: 12px; line-height: normal;"></span>Modes: Defines video modes
- <span class="s1" style="font-variant-numeric: normal; font-variant-east-asian: normal; font-variant-alternates: normal; font-kerning: auto; font-optical-sizing: auto; font-feature-settings: normal; font-variation-settings: normal; font-variant-position: normal; font-stretch: normal; font-size: 12px; line-height: normal;"></span>Device: Configures the session’s video card(s)
- <span class="s1" style="font-variant-numeric: normal; font-variant-east-asian: normal; font-variant-alternates: normal; font-kerning: auto; font-optical-sizing: auto; font-feature-settings: normal; font-variation-settings: normal; font-variant-position: normal; font-stretch: normal; font-size: 12px; line-height: normal;"></span>Screen: Sets the session’s screen resolution and color depth
- <span class="s1" style="font-variant-numeric: normal; font-variant-east-asian: normal; font-variant-alternates: normal; font-kerning: auto; font-optical-sizing: auto; font-feature-settings: normal; font-variation-settings: normal; font-variant-position: normal; font-stretch: normal; font-size: 12px; line-height: normal;"></span>Module: Denotes any modules that need to be loaded
- <span class="s1" style="font-variant-numeric: normal; font-variant-east-asian: normal; font-variant-alternates: normal; font-kerning: auto; font-optical-sizing: auto; font-feature-settings: normal; font-variation-settings: normal; font-variant-position: normal; font-stretch: normal; font-size: 12px; line-height: normal;"></span>Files: Sets file path names, if needed, for fonts, modules, and keyboard layout files
- <span class="s1" style="font-variant-numeric: normal; font-variant-east-asian: normal; font-variant-alternates: normal; font-kerning: auto; font-optical-sizing: auto; font-feature-settings: normal; font-variation-settings: normal; font-variant-position: normal; font-stretch: normal; font-size: 12px; line-height: normal;"></span>Server Flags: Configures global X server options
- <span class="s1" style="font-variant-numeric: normal; font-variant-east-asian: normal; font-variant-alternates: normal; font-kerning: auto; font-optical-sizing: auto; font-feature-settings: normal; font-variation-settings: normal; font-variant-position: normal; font-stretch: normal; font-size: 12px; line-height: normal;"></span>Server Layout: Links together all the session’s input and output devices

- <span class="s1" style="font-variant-numeric: normal; font-variant-east-asian: normal; font-variant-alternates: normal; font-kerning: auto; font-optical-sizing: auto; font-feature-settings: normal; font-variation-settings: normal; font-variant-position: normal; font-stretch: normal; font-size: 12px; line-height: normal;"></span>If something goes wrong with the display process, the X.Org server generates the .xsession-errors file in your Home directory (often referred to as ~/.xsession-errors).
- <span class="s1" style="font-variant-numeric: normal; font-variant-east-asian: normal; font-variant-alternates: normal; font-kerning: auto; font-optical-sizing: auto; font-feature-settings: normal; font-variation-settings: normal; font-variant-position: normal; font-stretch: normal; font-size: 12px; line-height: normal;"></span>two utilities are available that can help:

- <span class="s1" style="font-variant-numeric: normal; font-variant-east-asian: normal; font-variant-alternates: normal; font-kerning: auto; font-optical-sizing: auto; font-feature-settings: normal; font-variation-settings: normal; font-variant-position: normal; font-stretch: normal; font-size: 12px; line-height: normal;"></span>xdpyinfo: provides information about the X.Org server, including the different screen types available, the default communicate parameter values, protocol extension information, and so on.
- <span class="s1" style="font-variant-numeric: normal; font-variant-east-asian: normal; font-variant-alternates: normal; font-kerning: auto; font-optical-sizing: auto; font-feature-settings: normal; font-variation-settings: normal; font-variant-position: normal; font-stretch: normal; font-size: 12px; line-height: normal;"></span>xwininfo: Provides window information. If no options are given, an interactive utility asks you to click on the window for which you desir statistics.

Waynland

- <span class="s1" style="font-variant-numeric: normal; font-variant-east-asian: normal; font-variant-alternates: normal; font-kerning: auto; font-optical-sizing: auto; font-feature-settings: normal; font-variation-settings: normal; font-variant-position: normal; font-stretch: normal; font-size: 12px; line-height: normal;"></span>Waynland is designed to be simpler, more secure, and easier to develop and maintain than the X.Org software.
- <span class="s1" style="font-variant-numeric: normal; font-variant-east-asian: normal; font-variant-alternates: normal; font-kerning: auto; font-optical-sizing: auto; font-feature-settings: normal; font-variation-settings: normal; font-variant-position: normal; font-stretch: normal; font-size: 12px; line-height: normal;"></span>Waynland defines the communication protocol between a display server and its various clients. However, Wayland is also an umbrella term that covers the compositor, the window server, and the display server.
- <span class="s1" style="font-variant-numeric: normal; font-variant-east-asian: normal; font-variant-alternates: normal; font-kerning: auto; font-optical-sizing: auto; font-feature-settings: normal; font-variation-settings: normal; font-variant-position: normal; font-stretch: normal; font-size: 12px; line-height: normal;"></span>The Wayland compositor is Weston. However, Weston provides a rather basic desktop experience. It was created as a Wayland compositor reference implementation. (Weston was created to be a compositor requirements example for those developers who want to create their own Wayland compositor.) Weston’s core focus is correctness and reliability. Wayland’s compositor is swappable. you can use a different compositor if you need a more full-featured desktop experience. Several compositors are available for use with Wayland, including Arcan, Sway, Lipstick, and Clayland, to name a few.
- <span class="s1" style="font-variant-numeric: normal; font-variant-east-asian: normal; font-variant-alternates: normal; font-kerning: auto; font-optical-sizing: auto; font-feature-settings: normal; font-variation-settings: normal; font-variant-position: normal; font-stretch: normal; font-size: 12px; line-height: normal;"></span>Troubleshooting Wayland

- <span class="s1" style="font-variant-numeric: normal; font-variant-east-asian: normal; font-variant-alternates: normal; font-kerning: auto; font-optical-sizing: auto; font-feature-settings: normal; font-variation-settings: normal; font-variant-position: normal; font-stretch: normal; font-size: 12px; line-height: normal;"></span>Try the GUI without Wayland.: If your Linux distribution has multiple flavors of the desktop environment (with Wayland or with X11), log out of you GUI session and pick the desktop environment without Wayland. If your UI problems are resolved, then you know it has most likely something to do with Wayland.

- <span class="s1" style="font-variant-numeric: normal; font-variant-east-asian: normal; font-variant-alternates: normal; font-kerning: auto; font-optical-sizing: auto; font-feature-settings: normal; font-variation-settings: normal; font-variant-position: normal; font-stretch: normal; font-size: 12px; line-height: normal;"></span>If you do not have multiple flavors of the desktop environment and you are using the GNOME shell user interface, turn off Wayland by following these steps:

1.  Using super user privileges, edit the /etc/gdm3/custom.conf file.
2.  2\. Remove the # from the #WaylandEnable=false line and save the file.
3.  3\. Reboot the system and log in to a GUI session and see if the problems are gone.

- <span class="s1" style="font-variant-numeric: normal; font-variant-east-asian: normal; font-variant-alternates: normal; font-kerning: auto; font-optical-sizing: auto; font-feature-settings: normal; font-variation-settings: normal; font-variant-position: normal; font-stretch: normal; font-size: 12px; line-height: normal;"></span>Check your system’s graphics card: if your system seems to be running fine under X11 but gets problematic when running under Wayland, check your graphics card.
- <span class="s1" style="font-variant-numeric: normal; font-variant-east-asian: normal; font-variant-alternates: normal; font-kerning: auto; font-optical-sizing: auto; font-feature-settings: normal; font-variation-settings: normal; font-variant-position: normal; font-stretch: normal; font-size: 12px; line-height: normal;"></span>Use a different compositor: If you are using a desktop environment’s built-in compositor or one of the other compositors, try installing and using the Weston compositor package instead.

- <span class="s1" style="font-variant-numeric: normal; font-variant-east-asian: normal; font-variant-alternates: normal; font-kerning: auto; font-optical-sizing: auto; font-feature-settings: normal; font-variation-settings: normal; font-variant-position: normal; font-stretch: normal; font-size: 12px; line-height: normal;"></span>On Linux a GUI is a series of components that work together to provide the graphical setting for the UI. One of these components is the desktop environment.
- <span class="s1" style="font-variant-numeric: normal; font-variant-east-asian: normal; font-variant-alternates: normal; font-kerning: auto; font-optical-sizing: auto; font-feature-settings: normal; font-variation-settings: normal; font-variant-position: normal; font-stretch: normal; font-size: 12px; line-height: normal;"></span>A desktop environment provides a pre-determined look and feel to the GUI. It is typically broken up into the following graphical sections and functions:

- <span class="s1" style="font-variant-numeric: normal; font-variant-east-asian: normal; font-variant-alternates: normal; font-kerning: auto; font-optical-sizing: auto; font-feature-settings: normal; font-variation-settings: normal; font-variant-position: normal; font-stretch: normal; font-size: 12px; line-height: normal;"></span>Desktop Settings
- <span class="s1" style="font-variant-numeric: normal; font-variant-east-asian: normal; font-variant-alternates: normal; font-kerning: auto; font-optical-sizing: auto; font-feature-settings: normal; font-variation-settings: normal; font-variant-position: normal; font-stretch: normal; font-size: 12px; line-height: normal;"></span>Display Manager
- <span class="s1" style="font-variant-numeric: normal; font-variant-east-asian: normal; font-variant-alternates: normal; font-kerning: auto; font-optical-sizing: auto; font-feature-settings: normal; font-variation-settings: normal; font-variant-position: normal; font-stretch: normal; font-size: 12px; line-height: normal;"></span>File Manager
- <span class="s1" style="font-variant-numeric: normal; font-variant-east-asian: normal; font-variant-alternates: normal; font-kerning: auto; font-optical-sizing: auto; font-feature-settings: normal; font-variation-settings: normal; font-variant-position: normal; font-stretch: normal; font-size: 12px; line-height: normal;"></span>Icons
- <span class="s1" style="font-variant-numeric: normal; font-variant-east-asian: normal; font-variant-alternates: normal; font-kerning: auto; font-optical-sizing: auto; font-feature-settings: normal; font-variation-settings: normal; font-variant-position: normal; font-stretch: normal; font-size: 12px; line-height: normal;"></span>Favorites Bar
- <span class="s1" style="font-variant-numeric: normal; font-variant-east-asian: normal; font-variant-alternates: normal; font-kerning: auto; font-optical-sizing: auto; font-feature-settings: normal; font-variation-settings: normal; font-variant-position: normal; font-stretch: normal; font-size: 12px; line-height: normal;"></span>Launch
- <span class="s1" style="font-variant-numeric: normal; font-variant-east-asian: normal; font-variant-alternates: normal; font-kerning: auto; font-optical-sizing: auto; font-feature-settings: normal; font-variation-settings: normal; font-variant-position: normal; font-stretch: normal; font-size: 12px; line-height: normal;"></span>Menus
- <span class="s1" style="font-variant-numeric: normal; font-variant-east-asian: normal; font-variant-alternates: normal; font-kerning: auto; font-optical-sizing: auto; font-feature-settings: normal; font-variation-settings: normal; font-variant-position: normal; font-stretch: normal; font-size: 12px; line-height: normal;"></span>Panels
- <span class="s1" style="font-variant-numeric: normal; font-variant-east-asian: normal; font-variant-alternates: normal; font-kerning: auto; font-optical-sizing: auto; font-feature-settings: normal; font-variation-settings: normal; font-variant-position: normal; font-stretch: normal; font-size: 12px; line-height: normal;"></span>System Tray
- <span class="s1" style="font-variant-numeric: normal; font-variant-east-asian: normal; font-variant-alternates: normal; font-kerning: auto; font-optical-sizing: auto; font-feature-settings: normal; font-variation-settings: normal; font-variant-position: normal; font-stretch: normal; font-size: 12px; line-height: normal;"></span>Widgets
- <span class="s1" style="font-variant-numeric: normal; font-variant-east-asian: normal; font-variant-alternates: normal; font-kerning: auto; font-optical-sizing: auto; font-feature-settings: normal; font-variation-settings: normal; font-variant-position: normal; font-stretch: normal; font-size: 12px; line-height: normal;"></span>Windows Manager

- <span class="s1" style="font-variant-numeric: normal; font-variant-east-asian: normal; font-variant-alternates: normal; font-kerning: auto; font-optical-sizing: auto; font-feature-settings: normal; font-variation-settings: normal; font-variant-position: normal; font-stretch: normal; font-size: 12px; line-height: normal;"></span>The display manager component is responsible for controlling the graphical login feature. Every Linux display manager package uses the X Display Manager Control Protocol (XDMCP) to handle the graphical login process.
- <span class="s1" style="font-variant-numeric: normal; font-variant-east-asian: normal; font-variant-alternates: normal; font-kerning: auto; font-optical-sizing: auto; font-feature-settings: normal; font-variation-settings: normal; font-variant-position: normal; font-stretch: normal; font-size: 12px; line-height: normal;"></span>The X Display Manager (XDM) package is the basic display manager software available for Linux. It presents a generic user ID and password login screen, passing the login attempt off to the Linux system for verification. If the system authenticates the login attempt, XDM starts up the appropriate X server environment and Windows desktop environment.
- <span class="s1" style="font-variant-numeric: normal; font-variant-east-asian: normal; font-variant-alternates: normal; font-kerning: auto; font-optical-sizing: auto; font-feature-settings: normal; font-variation-settings: normal; font-variant-position: normal; font-stretch: normal; font-size: 12px; line-height: normal;"></span>/etc/X11/xdm/xdm-config —> XDM display manager is somewhat generic, there are some configuration features you can modify to change things a bit. In most situations, you’ll never need to modify any of these settings.
- <span class="s1" style="font-variant-numeric: normal; font-variant-east-asian: normal; font-variant-alternates: normal; font-kerning: auto; font-optical-sizing: auto; font-feature-settings: normal; font-variation-settings: normal; font-variant-position: normal; font-stretch: normal; font-size: 12px; line-height: normal;"></span>Most window managers create their own display manager and expand the capabilities of the XDM display manager. a few of the more popular display managers you’ll see:

- <span class="s1" style="font-variant-numeric: normal; font-variant-east-asian: normal; font-variant-alternates: normal; font-kerning: auto; font-optical-sizing: auto; font-feature-settings: normal; font-variation-settings: normal; font-variant-position: normal; font-stretch: normal; font-size: 12px; line-height: normal;"></span>KDM: The default display manager used by the KDE desktop environment
- <span class="s1" style="font-variant-numeric: normal; font-variant-east-asian: normal; font-variant-alternates: normal; font-kerning: auto; font-optical-sizing: auto; font-feature-settings: normal; font-variation-settings: normal; font-variant-position: normal; font-stretch: normal; font-size: 12px; line-height: normal;"></span>GDM: The default display manager used by the GNOME desktop environment
- <span class="s1" style="font-variant-numeric: normal; font-variant-east-asian: normal; font-variant-alternates: normal; font-kerning: auto; font-optical-sizing: auto; font-feature-settings: normal; font-variation-settings: normal; font-variant-position: normal; font-stretch: normal; font-size: 12px; line-height: normal;"></span>LightDM: A bare-bones display manager used in lightweight desktop environments such as Xfce

- <span class="s1" style="font-variant-numeric: normal; font-variant-east-asian: normal; font-variant-alternates: normal; font-kerning: auto; font-optical-sizing: auto; font-feature-settings: normal; font-variation-settings: normal; font-variant-position: normal; font-stretch: normal; font-size: 12px; line-height: normal;"></span>The X11 system utilizes a classic client/server model for serving up graphical desktops. In most situations, the client and server both run on the same physical device, but that doesn’t need to be the case.
- <span class="s1" style="font-variant-numeric: normal; font-variant-east-asian: normal; font-variant-alternates: normal; font-kerning: auto; font-optical-sizing: auto; font-feature-settings: normal; font-variation-settings: normal; font-variant-position: normal; font-stretch: normal; font-size: 12px; line-height: normal;"></span>X11 forwarding allows you to interact with various X11-based graphical utilities on a remote system through an encrypted network connection. This method is enacted using the openSSH service. First you need to check to see if X11 forwarding is permitted. This setting is in the openSSHconfiguration file, /etc/ssh/sshd_config. The directive X11Forwarding should be set to yes in the remote system’s configuration file. now the command to use is $ ssh -X user@remote-host
- <span class="s1" style="font-variant-numeric: normal; font-variant-east-asian: normal; font-variant-alternates: normal; font-kerning: auto; font-optical-sizing: auto; font-feature-settings: normal; font-variation-settings: normal; font-variant-position: normal; font-stretch: normal; font-size: 12px; line-height: normal;"></span>Remote Desktop Software

- <span class="s1" style="font-variant-numeric: normal; font-variant-east-asian: normal; font-variant-alternates: normal; font-kerning: auto; font-optical-sizing: auto; font-feature-settings: normal; font-variation-settings: normal; font-variant-position: normal; font-stretch: normal; font-size: 12px; line-height: normal;"></span>Virtual network computing (VNC): is multiplatform and employs the Remote Frame Buffer (RFB) protocol. This protocol allows a user on the client side to send GUI commands, such as mouse clicks, to the server. The server sends desktop frames back to the client’s monitor. The VNC server offers a GUI service at TCP port 5900+n, where n equals the display number, usually 1 (port 5901). The VNC server is flexible in that you can also use a Java-enabled web browser to access it. It provides that service at TCP port 5800+n. HTML5 client web browsers are supported as well. The following are positive benefits when using VNC:

- <span class="s1" style="font-variant-numeric: normal; font-variant-east-asian: normal; font-variant-alternates: normal; font-kerning: auto; font-optical-sizing: auto; font-feature-settings: normal; font-variation-settings: normal; font-variant-position: normal; font-stretch: normal; font-size: 12px; line-height: normal;"></span>It has lots of flexibility in providing remote desktops.
- <span class="s1" style="font-variant-numeric: normal; font-variant-east-asian: normal; font-variant-alternates: normal; font-kerning: auto; font-optical-sizing: auto; font-feature-settings: normal; font-variation-settings: normal; font-variant-position: normal; font-stretch: normal; font-size: 12px; line-height: normal;"></span>Desktops are available for multiple users.
- <span class="s1" style="font-variant-numeric: normal; font-variant-east-asian: normal; font-variant-alternates: normal; font-kerning: auto; font-optical-sizing: auto; font-feature-settings: normal; font-variation-settings: normal; font-variant-position: normal; font-stretch: normal; font-size: 12px; line-height: normal;"></span>Both persistent and static desktops are available.
- <span class="s1" style="font-variant-numeric: normal; font-variant-east-asian: normal; font-variant-alternates: normal; font-kerning: auto; font-optical-sizing: auto; font-feature-settings: normal; font-variation-settings: normal; font-variant-position: normal; font-stretch: normal; font-size: 12px; line-height: normal;"></span>It can provide desktops on an on-demand basis.
- <span class="s1" style="font-variant-numeric: normal; font-variant-east-asian: normal; font-variant-alternates: normal; font-kerning: auto; font-optical-sizing: auto; font-feature-settings: normal; font-variation-settings: normal; font-variant-position: normal; font-stretch: normal; font-size: 12px; line-height: normal;"></span>An SSH tunnel can be employed via ssh or a client viewer command-line option to encrypt traffic.

- <span class="s1" style="font-variant-numeric: normal; font-variant-east-asian: normal; font-variant-alternates: normal; font-kerning: auto; font-optical-sizing: auto; font-feature-settings: normal; font-variation-settings: normal; font-variant-position: normal; font-stretch: normal; font-size: 12px; line-height: normal;"></span>The following are potential difficulties or concerns with VNC:

- <span class="s1" style="font-variant-numeric: normal; font-variant-east-asian: normal; font-variant-alternates: normal; font-kerning: auto; font-optical-sizing: auto; font-feature-settings: normal; font-variation-settings: normal; font-variant-position: normal; font-stretch: normal; font-size: 12px; line-height: normal;"></span>The VNC server handles only mouse movements and keystrokes. It does not deal with file an audio transfer or printing services for the client.
- <span class="s1" style="font-variant-numeric: normal; font-variant-east-asian: normal; font-variant-alternates: normal; font-kerning: auto; font-optical-sizing: auto; font-feature-settings: normal; font-variation-settings: normal; font-variant-position: normal; font-stretch: normal; font-size: 12px; line-height: normal;"></span>VNC, by default, does not provide traffic encryption, so you must employ another means of protection, such as tunneling through openSSH.
- <span class="s1" style="font-variant-numeric: normal; font-variant-east-asian: normal; font-variant-alternates: normal; font-kerning: auto; font-optical-sizing: auto; font-feature-settings: normal; font-variation-settings: normal; font-variant-position: normal; font-stretch: normal; font-size: 12px; line-height: normal;"></span>The VNC server password is stored as plaintext in a server file.

- <span class="s1" style="font-variant-numeric: normal; font-variant-east-asian: normal; font-variant-alternates: normal; font-kerning: auto; font-optical-sizing: auto; font-feature-settings: normal; font-variation-settings: normal; font-variant-position: normal; font-stretch: normal; font-size: 12px; line-height: normal;"></span>TigerVNC
- <span class="s1" style="font-variant-numeric: normal; font-variant-east-asian: normal; font-variant-alternates: normal; font-kerning: auto; font-optical-sizing: auto; font-feature-settings: normal; font-variation-settings: normal; font-variant-position: normal; font-stretch: normal; font-size: 12px; line-height: normal;"></span>Xrdp: supports the Remote Desktop Protocol (RDP) and uses X11rdp or Xvnc to manage the GUI session. Xrdp provides only the server side of an RDP connection. It allows access from several RDP client implementations, such as rdesktop, FreeFDP, and Microsoft Remote Desktop Connection. positive benefits of using Xrdp:

- <span class="s1" style="font-variant-numeric: normal; font-variant-east-asian: normal; font-variant-alternates: normal; font-kerning: auto; font-optical-sizing: auto; font-feature-settings: normal; font-variation-settings: normal; font-variant-position: normal; font-stretch: normal; font-size: 12px; line-height: normal;"></span>Xrdp uses RDP, which encrypts its traffic using Transport Layer Security (TLS).
- <span class="s1" style="font-variant-numeric: normal; font-variant-east-asian: normal; font-variant-alternates: normal; font-kerning: auto; font-optical-sizing: auto; font-feature-settings: normal; font-variation-settings: normal; font-variant-position: normal; font-stretch: normal; font-size: 12px; line-height: normal;"></span>A wide variety of open source RDP client software is available.
- <span class="s1" style="font-variant-numeric: normal; font-variant-east-asian: normal; font-variant-alternates: normal; font-kerning: auto; font-optical-sizing: auto; font-feature-settings: normal; font-variation-settings: normal; font-variant-position: normal; font-stretch: normal; font-size: 12px; line-height: normal;"></span>You can connect to an already existing connection to provide a persistent desktop.
- <span class="s1" style="font-variant-numeric: normal; font-variant-east-asian: normal; font-variant-alternates: normal; font-kerning: auto; font-optical-sizing: auto; font-feature-settings: normal; font-variation-settings: normal; font-variant-position: normal; font-stretch: normal; font-size: 12px; line-height: normal;"></span>The Xrdp server handles mouse movements and keystrokes as well as with audio transfers and mounting of local client drives on the remote system.

- <span class="s1" style="font-variant-numeric: normal; font-variant-east-asian: normal; font-variant-alternates: normal; font-kerning: auto; font-optical-sizing: auto; font-feature-settings: normal; font-variation-settings: normal; font-variant-position: normal; font-stretch: normal; font-size: 12px; line-height: normal;"></span>/etc/xrdp/xrdp.ini —> determine the various Xrdp configuration settings. An important setting in this file is the security_layer directive.

- <span class="s1" style="font-variant-numeric: normal; font-variant-east-asian: normal; font-variant-alternates: normal; font-kerning: auto; font-optical-sizing: auto; font-feature-settings: normal; font-variation-settings: normal; font-variant-position: normal; font-stretch: normal; font-size: 12px; line-height: normal;"></span>NX protocol (sometimes called NX technology): positive benefits of using NX products:

- <span class="s1" style="font-variant-numeric: normal; font-variant-east-asian: normal; font-variant-alternates: normal; font-kerning: auto; font-optical-sizing: auto; font-feature-settings: normal; font-variation-settings: normal; font-variant-position: normal; font-stretch: normal; font-size: 12px; line-height: normal;"></span>They provide excellent response times even over low-bandwidth connections that have high-latency issues.
- <span class="s1" style="font-variant-numeric: normal; font-variant-east-asian: normal; font-variant-alternates: normal; font-kerning: auto; font-optical-sizing: auto; font-feature-settings: normal; font-variation-settings: normal; font-variant-position: normal; font-stretch: normal; font-size: 12px; line-height: normal;"></span>They are faster than VNC-based products.
- <span class="s1" style="font-variant-numeric: normal; font-variant-east-asian: normal; font-variant-alternates: normal; font-kerning: auto; font-optical-sizing: auto; font-feature-settings: normal; font-variation-settings: normal; font-variant-position: normal; font-stretch: normal; font-size: 12px; line-height: normal;"></span>They use openSSH tunneling by default, so traffic is encrypted.
- <span class="s1" style="font-variant-numeric: normal; font-variant-east-asian: normal; font-variant-alternates: normal; font-kerning: auto; font-optical-sizing: auto; font-feature-settings: normal; font-variation-settings: normal; font-variant-position: normal; font-stretch: normal; font-size: 12px; line-height: normal;"></span>They support multiple simultaneous users through a single network port.
- <span class="s1" style="font-variant-numeric: normal; font-variant-east-asian: normal; font-variant-alternates: normal; font-kerning: auto; font-optical-sizing: auto; font-feature-settings: normal; font-variation-settings: normal; font-variant-position: normal; font-stretch: normal; font-size: 12px; line-height: normal;"></span>NX technology compresses the X11 data so that there is less data to send over the network, which improves response times.
- <span class="s1" style="font-variant-numeric: normal; font-variant-east-asian: normal; font-variant-alternates: normal; font-kerning: auto; font-optical-sizing: auto; font-feature-settings: normal; font-variation-settings: normal; font-variant-position: normal; font-stretch: normal; font-size: 12px; line-height: normal;"></span>It also heavily employs caching data to provide an improved remote desktop experience.

- <span class="s1" style="font-variant-numeric: normal; font-variant-east-asian: normal; font-variant-alternates: normal; font-kerning: auto; font-optical-sizing: auto; font-feature-settings: normal; font-variation-settings: normal; font-variant-position: normal; font-stretch: normal; font-size: 12px; line-height: normal;"></span>Simple Protocol for Independent Computing Environments (SPICE): typically Spice is used for providing connections with KVM virtual machines, moving into VNC’s territory. some nice features:

- <span class="s1" style="font-variant-numeric: normal; font-variant-east-asian: normal; font-variant-alternates: normal; font-kerning: auto; font-optical-sizing: auto; font-feature-settings: normal; font-variation-settings: normal; font-variant-position: normal; font-stretch: normal; font-size: 12px; line-height: normal;"></span>Spice’s client side uses multiple data socket connections, and you can have multiple clients.
- <span class="s1" style="font-variant-numeric: normal; font-variant-east-asian: normal; font-variant-alternates: normal; font-kerning: auto; font-optical-sizing: auto; font-feature-settings: normal; font-variation-settings: normal; font-variant-position: normal; font-stretch: normal; font-size: 12px; line-height: normal;"></span>Spice delivers desktop experience speeds similar to a local connection.
- <span class="s1" style="font-variant-numeric: normal; font-variant-east-asian: normal; font-variant-alternates: normal; font-kerning: auto; font-optical-sizing: auto; font-feature-settings: normal; font-variation-settings: normal; font-variant-position: normal; font-stretch: normal; font-size: 12px; line-height: normal;"></span>Spice consumes low amounts of CPU, so you can use it with various servers that have multiple virtual machines and not adversely affect their performance.
- <span class="s1" style="font-variant-numeric: normal; font-variant-east-asian: normal; font-variant-alternates: normal; font-kerning: auto; font-optical-sizing: auto; font-feature-settings: normal; font-variation-settings: normal; font-variant-position: normal; font-stretch: normal; font-size: 12px; line-height: normal;"></span>Spice allows high-quality video streaming.
- <span class="s1" style="font-variant-numeric: normal; font-variant-east-asian: normal; font-variant-alternates: normal; font-kerning: auto; font-optical-sizing: auto; font-feature-settings: normal; font-variation-settings: normal; font-variant-position: normal; font-stretch: normal; font-size: 12px; line-height: normal;"></span>Spice provides live migration features, which means there are no connection interruptions if the virtual machine is being migrated to a new host.

———————————————

**Administering the System:**

Locale

- <span class="s1" style="font-variant-numeric: normal; font-variant-east-asian: normal; font-variant-alternates: normal; font-kerning: auto; font-optical-sizing: auto; font-feature-settings: normal; font-variation-settings: normal; font-variant-position: normal; font-stretch: normal; font-size: 12px; line-height: normal;"></span>Not only does each country have its own language (or sometimes, sets of languages), but each country also has its own way in which people write numerical values, monetary values, and the time and date. For a Linux system to be useful in any specific location, it must adapt to the local way of doing all those things.
- <span class="s1" style="font-variant-numeric: normal; font-variant-east-asian: normal; font-variant-alternates: normal; font-kerning: auto; font-optical-sizing: auto; font-feature-settings: normal; font-variation-settings: normal; font-variant-position: normal; font-stretch: normal; font-size: 12px; line-height: normal;"></span>A character set defines a standard code used to interpret and display characters in a language.

- <span class="s1" style="font-variant-numeric: normal; font-variant-east-asian: normal; font-variant-alternates: normal; font-kerning: auto; font-optical-sizing: auto; font-feature-settings: normal; font-variation-settings: normal; font-variant-position: normal; font-stretch: normal; font-size: 12px; line-height: normal;"></span>ASCII: The American Standard Code for Information Interchange (ASCII) uses 7 bits to store characters found in the English language.
- <span class="s1" style="font-variant-numeric: normal; font-variant-east-asian: normal; font-variant-alternates: normal; font-kerning: auto; font-optical-sizing: auto; font-feature-settings: normal; font-variation-settings: normal; font-variant-position: normal; font-stretch: normal; font-size: 12px; line-height: normal;"></span>ISO-8859: The International Organization for Standardization (ISO) worked with the International Electrotechnical Commission (IEC) to produce a series of standard codes for handling international characters. There are 15 separate standards (ISO-8859-1 through ISO-8859-15) for defining different character sets.
- <span class="s1" style="font-variant-numeric: normal; font-variant-east-asian: normal; font-variant-alternates: normal; font-kerning: auto; font-optical-sizing: auto; font-feature-settings: normal; font-variation-settings: normal; font-variant-position: normal; font-stretch: normal; font-size: 12px; line-height: normal;"></span>Unicode: The Unicode Consortium, composed of many computing industry companies, created an international standard that uses a 3-byte code and can represent every character known to be in use in all countries of the world.
- <span class="s1" style="font-variant-numeric: normal; font-variant-east-asian: normal; font-variant-alternates: normal; font-kerning: auto; font-optical-sizing: auto; font-feature-settings: normal; font-variation-settings: normal; font-variant-position: normal; font-stretch: normal; font-size: 12px; line-height: normal;"></span>UTF: Unicode Transformation Format (UTF) transforms the long Unicode values into either 1-byte (UTF-8) or 2-byte (UTF-16) simplified codes. For work in English-speaking countries, the UTF-8 character set is replacing ASCII as the standard.

- <span class="s1" style="font-variant-numeric: normal; font-variant-east-asian: normal; font-variant-alternates: normal; font-kerning: auto; font-optical-sizing: auto; font-feature-settings: normal; font-variation-settings: normal; font-variant-position: normal; font-stretch: normal; font-size: 12px; line-height: normal;"></span>$ locale —> get locale-specific environmental variables. The output of the locale command is in the format: language_country.character set
- <span class="s1" style="font-variant-numeric: normal; font-variant-east-asian: normal; font-variant-alternates: normal; font-kerning: auto; font-optical-sizing: auto; font-feature-settings: normal; font-variation-settings: normal; font-variant-position: normal; font-stretch: normal; font-size: 12px; line-height: normal;"></span>for changing locales

- <span class="s1" style="font-variant-numeric: normal; font-variant-east-asian: normal; font-variant-alternates: normal; font-kerning: auto; font-optical-sizing: auto; font-feature-settings: normal; font-variation-settings: normal; font-variant-position: normal; font-stretch: normal; font-size: 12px; line-height: normal;"></span>changing manually: (changes the localization for your current login session)

- <span class="s1" style="font-variant-numeric: normal; font-variant-east-asian: normal; font-variant-alternates: normal; font-kerning: auto; font-optical-sizing: auto; font-feature-settings: normal; font-variation-settings: normal; font-variant-position: normal; font-stretch: normal; font-size: 12px; line-height: normal;"></span>using $ export ,<span class="Apple-converted-space"> </span>
- <span class="s1" style="font-variant-numeric: normal; font-variant-east-asian: normal; font-variant-alternates: normal; font-kerning: auto; font-optical-sizing: auto; font-feature-settings: normal; font-variation-settings: normal; font-variant-position: normal; font-stretch: normal; font-size: 12px; line-height: normal;"></span>Instead of having to change all of the LC\_ environment variables individually, the LANG environment variable controls all of them at one place

- <span class="s1" style="font-variant-numeric: normal; font-variant-east-asian: normal; font-variant-alternates: normal; font-kerning: auto; font-optical-sizing: auto; font-feature-settings: normal; font-variation-settings: normal; font-variant-position: normal; font-stretch: normal; font-size: 12px; line-height: normal;"></span>$ localectl —> Control the system locale and keyboard layout settings.

Time

- <span class="s1" style="font-variant-numeric: normal; font-variant-east-asian: normal; font-variant-alternates: normal; font-kerning: auto; font-optical-sizing: auto; font-feature-settings: normal; font-variation-settings: normal; font-variant-position: normal; font-stretch: normal; font-size: 12px; line-height: normal;"></span>Many elements depend on accurate time, such as programs designed to run at particular moments, remote services that expect accurate client times (and will reject the client if their times are inaccurate), and maintaining accurate log message time stamps in order to properly investigate client/server issues.
- <span class="s1" style="font-variant-numeric: normal; font-variant-east-asian: normal; font-variant-alternates: normal; font-kerning: auto; font-optical-sizing: auto; font-feature-settings: normal; font-variation-settings: normal; font-variant-position: normal; font-stretch: normal; font-size: 12px; line-height: normal;"></span>Local time is also called wall clock time.
- <span class="s1" style="font-variant-numeric: normal; font-variant-east-asian: normal; font-variant-alternates: normal; font-kerning: auto; font-optical-sizing: auto; font-feature-settings: normal; font-variation-settings: normal; font-variant-position: normal; font-stretch: normal; font-size: 12px; line-height: normal;"></span>It’s often easier to use a different standard called Coordinated Universal Time (UTC). UTC is a time that does not change according to an individual’s time zone.
- <span class="s1" style="font-variant-numeric: normal; font-variant-east-asian: normal; font-variant-alternates: normal; font-kerning: auto; font-optical-sizing: auto; font-feature-settings: normal; font-variation-settings: normal; font-variant-position: normal; font-stretch: normal; font-size: 12px; line-height: normal;"></span>Linux maintains two time clocks:

- <span class="s1" style="font-variant-numeric: normal; font-variant-east-asian: normal; font-variant-alternates: normal; font-kerning: auto; font-optical-sizing: auto; font-feature-settings: normal; font-variation-settings: normal; font-variant-position: normal; font-stretch: normal; font-size: 12px; line-height: normal;"></span>hardware based: also called the real-time clock. attempts to maintain the correct time, even when the system is powered down by using power from the system battery (traditionally called the CMOS battery). When the system boots, the Linux OS gets the time from the hardware clock and updates its software clock.
- <span class="s1" style="font-variant-numeric: normal; font-variant-east-asian: normal; font-variant-alternates: normal; font-kerning: auto; font-optical-sizing: auto; font-feature-settings: normal; font-variation-settings: normal; font-variant-position: normal; font-stretch: normal; font-size: 12px; line-height: normal;"></span>software based: This clock runs only while the system is up and is used by many utilities on Linux, which is why it is sometimes called system time. Unfortunately the Linux software clock has a tendency to become inaccurate, especially if it is a busy system.

- <span class="s1" style="font-variant-numeric: normal; font-variant-east-asian: normal; font-variant-alternates: normal; font-kerning: auto; font-optical-sizing: auto; font-feature-settings: normal; font-variation-settings: normal; font-variant-position: normal; font-stretch: normal; font-size: 12px; line-height: normal;"></span>Each country selects one or more time zones, or offsets from the standard Coordinated Universal Time (UTC) time, to determine time within the country.
- <span class="s1" style="font-variant-numeric: normal; font-variant-east-asian: normal; font-variant-alternates: normal; font-kerning: auto; font-optical-sizing: auto; font-feature-settings: normal; font-variation-settings: normal; font-variant-position: normal; font-stretch: normal; font-size: 12px; line-height: normal;"></span>/etc/timezone (Debian-based) & /etc/localtime (Red Hat–based) —> These files are not in a text format, so you can’t simply edit. To change the time zone for a Linux system, copy or link the appropriate time zone template file from the /usr/share/zoneinfo folder to the /etc/timezone or /etc/localtime location. e.g: /usr/share/zoneinfo/US/Eastern.
- <span class="s1" style="font-variant-numeric: normal; font-variant-east-asian: normal; font-variant-alternates: normal; font-kerning: auto; font-optical-sizing: auto; font-feature-settings: normal; font-variation-settings: normal; font-variant-position: normal; font-stretch: normal; font-size: 12px; line-height: normal;"></span>$ hwclock —> time clocks utility
- <span class="s1" style="font-variant-numeric: normal; font-variant-east-asian: normal; font-variant-alternates: normal; font-kerning: auto; font-optical-sizing: auto; font-feature-settings: normal; font-variation-settings: normal; font-variant-position: normal; font-stretch: normal; font-size: 12px; line-height: normal;"></span>$ date —> display or set the time and date in a multitude of formats
- <span class="s1" style="font-variant-numeric: normal; font-variant-east-asian: normal; font-variant-alternates: normal; font-kerning: auto; font-optical-sizing: auto; font-feature-settings: normal; font-variation-settings: normal; font-variant-position: normal; font-stretch: normal; font-size: 12px; line-height: normal;"></span>$ timedatectl —> Control the system time and date
- <span class="s1" style="font-variant-numeric: normal; font-variant-east-asian: normal; font-variant-alternates: normal; font-kerning: auto; font-optical-sizing: auto; font-feature-settings: normal; font-variation-settings: normal; font-variant-position: normal; font-stretch: normal; font-size: 12px; line-height: normal;"></span>Network Time Protocol (NTP): a network protocol used to synchronize clocks over a network in order to provide accurate time. NTP uses what is called a clock stratum scheme. The stratums are numbered from 0 to 15\. The devices at stratum 0 are highly accurate time-keeping hardware devices, such as atomic clocks. The next level down is stratum 1, which consists of computers that are directly connected to the stratum 0 devices.
- <span class="s1" style="font-variant-numeric: normal; font-variant-east-asian: normal; font-variant-alternates: normal; font-kerning: auto; font-optical-sizing: auto; font-feature-settings: normal; font-variation-settings: normal; font-variant-position: normal; font-stretch: normal; font-size: 12px; line-height: normal;"></span>One of the most popular NTP servers is actually a cluster of servers that work together in what is called a pool. To use the NTP server pool, when you configure your NTP client application, enter pool.ntp.org as your NTP server.
- <span class="s1" style="font-variant-numeric: normal; font-variant-east-asian: normal; font-variant-alternates: normal; font-kerning: auto; font-optical-sizing: auto; font-feature-settings: normal; font-variation-settings: normal; font-variant-position: normal; font-stretch: normal; font-size: 12px; line-height: normal;"></span>An interesting time problem revolves around leap seconds. Because the earth’s rotation has been slowing down, our actual day is about 0.001 seconds less than 24 hours. About every 19 months or so, NTP passes a leap second announcement. This is typically handled without any problems and the clocks are set backward by one second. some applications have problems, Google introduced free public time servers that use NTP and smear the leap second over the course of time so that there is no need to issue a leap second announcement. This is called leap-smearing. The Google leap-smearing NTP servers are timen .google.com, where nis set to 1 through 4.
- <span class="s1" style="font-variant-numeric: normal; font-variant-east-asian: normal; font-variant-alternates: normal; font-kerning: auto; font-optical-sizing: auto; font-feature-settings: normal; font-variation-settings: normal; font-variant-position: normal; font-stretch: normal; font-size: 12px; line-height: normal;"></span>If you need to implement an NTP client program, you have choices.

- <span class="s1" style="font-variant-numeric: normal; font-variant-east-asian: normal; font-variant-alternates: normal; font-kerning: auto; font-optical-sizing: auto; font-feature-settings: normal; font-variation-settings: normal; font-variant-position: normal; font-stretch: normal; font-size: 12px; line-height: normal;"></span>You can either employ the NTP daemon (ntpd)
- <span class="s1" style="font-variant-numeric: normal; font-variant-east-asian: normal; font-variant-alternates: normal; font-kerning: auto; font-optical-sizing: auto; font-feature-settings: normal; font-variation-settings: normal; font-variant-position: normal; font-stretch: normal; font-size: 12px; line-height: normal;"></span>or use the newer chrony daemon (chronyd).

- <span class="s1" style="font-variant-numeric: normal; font-variant-east-asian: normal; font-variant-alternates: normal; font-kerning: auto; font-optical-sizing: auto; font-feature-settings: normal; font-variation-settings: normal; font-variant-position: normal; font-stretch: normal; font-size: 12px; line-height: normal;"></span>For years the NTP program was synonymous with the network time protocol, and on Linux they were often spoken of interchangeably. But it does have some limitations, such as keeping time accurate when the network has high traffic volumes, which is why alternatives such as chrony were developed. The NTP program is installed by default on some distributions and not on others. The package name is ntp, so you can check to see if it is installed
- <span class="s1" style="font-variant-numeric: normal; font-variant-east-asian: normal; font-variant-alternates: normal; font-kerning: auto; font-optical-sizing: auto; font-feature-settings: normal; font-variation-settings: normal; font-variant-position: normal; font-stretch: normal; font-size: 12px; line-height: normal;"></span>/etc/ntp.conf —> It contains, among other directives, the NTP time servers you wish to use.The directive name for setting these, On CentOS is server & On Ubuntu is pool
- <span class="s1" style="font-variant-numeric: normal; font-variant-east-asian: normal; font-variant-alternates: normal; font-kerning: auto; font-optical-sizing: auto; font-feature-settings: normal; font-variation-settings: normal; font-variant-position: normal; font-stretch: normal; font-size: 12px; line-height: normal;"></span>$ ntpq -p —> view a table showing what time servers your ntpd is polling and when the last synchronization took place.

chronyd

- <span class="s1" style="font-variant-numeric: normal; font-variant-east-asian: normal; font-variant-alternates: normal; font-kerning: auto; font-optical-sizing: auto; font-feature-settings: normal; font-variation-settings: normal; font-variant-position: normal; font-stretch: normal; font-size: 12px; line-height: normal;"></span>The chrony daemon (chronyd) has many improvements over ntpd.

- <span class="s1" style="font-variant-numeric: normal; font-variant-east-asian: normal; font-variant-alternates: normal; font-kerning: auto; font-optical-sizing: auto; font-feature-settings: normal; font-variation-settings: normal; font-variant-position: normal; font-stretch: normal; font-size: 12px; line-height: normal;"></span>It can keep accurate time even on systems that have busy networks or that are down for periods of time, and even on virtualized systems.
- <span class="s1" style="font-variant-numeric: normal; font-variant-east-asian: normal; font-variant-alternates: normal; font-kerning: auto; font-optical-sizing: auto; font-feature-settings: normal; font-variation-settings: normal; font-variant-position: normal; font-stretch: normal; font-size: 12px; line-height: normal;"></span>it synchronizes the system clock faster than does ntpd, and it can easily be configured to act as a local time server itself.

- <span class="s1" style="font-variant-numeric: normal; font-variant-east-asian: normal; font-variant-alternates: normal; font-kerning: auto; font-optical-sizing: auto; font-feature-settings: normal; font-variation-settings: normal; font-variant-position: normal; font-stretch: normal; font-size: 12px; line-height: normal;"></span>The package name is chrony.<span class="Apple-converted-space"> </span>

- <span class="s1" style="font-variant-numeric: normal; font-variant-east-asian: normal; font-variant-alternates: normal; font-kerning: auto; font-optical-sizing: auto; font-feature-settings: normal; font-variation-settings: normal; font-variant-position: normal; font-stretch: normal; font-size: 12px; line-height: normal;"></span>on CentOS and other Red Hat–based distros that the chrony is installed by default, but not enabled on boot (by default). usesuper user privileges and type $ systemctl start chronyd at the command line.
- <span class="s1" style="font-variant-numeric: normal; font-variant-east-asian: normal; font-variant-alternates: normal; font-kerning: auto; font-optical-sizing: auto; font-feature-settings: normal; font-variation-settings: normal; font-variant-position: normal; font-stretch: normal; font-size: 12px; line-height: normal;"></span>on Ubuntu, when chrony is installed it is automatically started and enabled on boot.

- <span class="s1" style="font-variant-numeric: normal; font-variant-east-asian: normal; font-variant-alternates: normal; font-kerning: auto; font-optical-sizing: auto; font-feature-settings: normal; font-variation-settings: normal; font-variant-position: normal; font-stretch: normal; font-size: 12px; line-height: normal;"></span>/etc/chrony.conf or /etc/chrony/chrony.conf —> primary configuration file for chrony. The directive name for setting these is either server or pool. The server directive is typically used for a single time server designation. pool indicates a server pool. rtcsync directive directs chrony to periodically update the hardware time (real-time clock).
- <span class="s1" style="font-variant-numeric: normal; font-variant-east-asian: normal; font-variant-alternates: normal; font-kerning: auto; font-optical-sizing: auto; font-feature-settings: normal; font-variation-settings: normal; font-variant-position: normal; font-stretch: normal; font-size: 12px; line-height: normal;"></span>chronyc - command-line interface for chrony daemon

Users & Groups

- <span class="s1" style="font-variant-numeric: normal; font-variant-east-asian: normal; font-variant-alternates: normal; font-kerning: auto; font-optical-sizing: auto; font-feature-settings: normal; font-variation-settings: normal; font-variant-position: normal; font-stretch: normal; font-size: 12px; line-height: normal;"></span>User accounts and their underlying framework are at the center of credential management and access controls. These accounts are a part of Linux’s discretionary access control (DAC).
- <span class="s1" style="font-variant-numeric: normal; font-variant-east-asian: normal; font-variant-alternates: normal; font-kerning: auto; font-optical-sizing: auto; font-feature-settings: normal; font-variation-settings: normal; font-variant-position: normal; font-stretch: normal; font-size: 12px; line-height: normal;"></span>DAC is the traditional Linux security control, where access to a file, or any object, is based on the user’s identity and current group membership.
- <span class="s1" style="font-variant-numeric: normal; font-variant-east-asian: normal; font-variant-alternates: normal; font-kerning: auto; font-optical-sizing: auto; font-feature-settings: normal; font-variation-settings: normal; font-variant-position: normal; font-stretch: normal; font-size: 12px; line-height: normal;"></span>Though a user account can have lots of group memberships, its process can have only one designated current group at a time.

- <span class="s1" style="font-variant-numeric: normal; font-variant-east-asian: normal; font-variant-alternates: normal; font-kerning: auto; font-optical-sizing: auto; font-feature-settings: normal; font-variation-settings: normal; font-variant-position: normal; font-stretch: normal; font-size: 12px; line-height: normal;"></span>A user account, sometimes called a normal account, is any account, an authorized human with the appropriate credentials has been given to access the system and perform daily tasks.
- <span class="s1" style="font-variant-numeric: normal; font-variant-east-asian: normal; font-variant-alternates: normal; font-kerning: auto; font-optical-sizing: auto; font-feature-settings: normal; font-variation-settings: normal; font-variant-position: normal; font-stretch: normal; font-size: 12px; line-height: normal;"></span>A user ID (UID) is the number used by Linux to identify user accounts.
- <span class="s1" style="font-variant-numeric: normal; font-variant-east-asian: normal; font-variant-alternates: normal; font-kerning: auto; font-optical-sizing: auto; font-feature-settings: normal; font-variation-settings: normal; font-variant-position: normal; font-stretch: normal; font-size: 12px; line-height: normal;"></span>System accounts are accounts that provide services (daemons) or perform special tasks, such as the root user account.
- <span class="s1" style="font-variant-numeric: normal; font-variant-east-asian: normal; font-variant-alternates: normal; font-kerning: auto; font-optical-sizing: auto; font-feature-settings: normal; font-variation-settings: normal; font-variant-position: normal; font-stretch: normal; font-size: 12px; line-height: normal;"></span>root UID is 0.
- <span class="s1" style="font-variant-numeric: normal; font-variant-east-asian: normal; font-variant-alternates: normal; font-kerning: auto; font-optical-sizing: auto; font-feature-settings: normal; font-variation-settings: normal; font-variant-position: normal; font-stretch: normal; font-size: 12px; line-height: normal;"></span>/etc/login.defs —> typically installed by default on most Linux distributions. contains directives for use in various shadow password suite commands. such as the useradd, userdel, and passwd commands. The directives in this configuration file control: password length, how long until the user is required to change the account’s password, whether or not a home directory is created by default, and so on. The file is typically filled with comments and commented-out directives.

<table cellspacing="0" cellpadding="0" class="t1" style="border-collapse: collapse;">

<tbody>

<tr>

<td valign="top" class="td1" style="border-style: solid; border-width: 1px; border-color: rgb(154, 154, 154); padding: 1px 5px;">

Name

</td>

<td valign="top" class="td1" style="border-style: solid; border-width: 1px; border-color: rgb(154, 154, 154); padding: 1px 5px;">

Desc

</td>

</tr>

<tr>

<td valign="top" class="td1" style="border-style: solid; border-width: 1px; border-color: rgb(154, 154, 154); padding: 1px 5px;">

PASS_MAX_DAYS

</td>

<td valign="top" class="td1" style="border-style: solid; border-width: 1px; border-color: rgb(154, 154, 154); padding: 1px 5px;">

Number of days until a password change is required. This is the password’s expiration date.

</td>

</tr>

<tr>

<td valign="top" class="td1" style="border-style: solid; border-width: 1px; border-color: rgb(154, 154, 154); padding: 1px 5px;">

PASS_MIN_DAYS

</td>

<td valign="top" class="td1" style="border-style: solid; border-width: 1px; border-color: rgb(154, 154, 154); padding: 1px 5px;">

Number of days after a password is changed until the password may be changed again.

</td>

</tr>

<tr>

<td valign="top" class="td1" style="border-style: solid; border-width: 1px; border-color: rgb(154, 154, 154); padding: 1px 5px;">

PASS_MIN_LENGT

</td>

<td valign="top" class="td1" style="border-style: solid; border-width: 1px; border-color: rgb(154, 154, 154); padding: 1px 5px;">

Minimum number of characters required in password.

</td>

</tr>

<tr>

<td valign="top" class="td1" style="border-style: solid; border-width: 1px; border-color: rgb(154, 154, 154); padding: 1px 5px;">

PASS_WARN_AGE

</td>

<td valign="top" class="td1" style="border-style: solid; border-width: 1px; border-color: rgb(154, 154, 154); padding: 1px 5px;">

Number of days a warning is issued to the user prior to a password’s expiration.

</td>

</tr>

<tr>

<td valign="top" class="td1" style="border-style: solid; border-width: 1px; border-color: rgb(154, 154, 154); padding: 1px 5px;">

CREATE_HOME

</td>

<td valign="top" class="td1" style="border-style: solid; border-width: 1px; border-color: rgb(154, 154, 154); padding: 1px 5px;">

Default is no. If set to yes, a user account home directory is created.

</td>

</tr>

<tr>

<td valign="top" class="td1" style="border-style: solid; border-width: 1px; border-color: rgb(154, 154, 154); padding: 1px 5px;">

ENCRYPT_METHOD

</td>

<td valign="top" class="td1" style="border-style: solid; border-width: 1px; border-color: rgb(154, 154, 154); padding: 1px 5px;">

The method used to hash account passwords.

</td>

</tr>

<tr>

<td valign="top" class="td1" style="border-style: solid; border-width: 1px; border-color: rgb(154, 154, 154); padding: 1px 5px;">

UID_MIN

</td>

<td valign="top" class="td1" style="border-style: solid; border-width: 1px; border-color: rgb(154, 154, 154); padding: 1px 5px;">

Indicates the lowest UID allowed for user accounts.

</td>

</tr>

<tr>

<td valign="top" class="td1" style="border-style: solid; border-width: 1px; border-color: rgb(154, 154, 154); padding: 1px 5px;">

SYS_UID_MIN

</td>

<td valign="top" class="td1" style="border-style: solid; border-width: 1px; border-color: rgb(154, 154, 154); padding: 1px 5px;">

A system account’s minimum UID

</td>

</tr>

</tbody>
