</table>

- <span class="s1" style="font-variant-numeric: normal; font-variant-east-asian: normal; font-variant-alternates: normal; font-kerning: auto; font-optical-sizing: auto; font-feature-settings: normal; font-variation-settings: normal; font-variant-position: normal; font-stretch: normal; font-size: 12px; line-height: normal;"></span>The syslog protocol severity values

<table cellspacing="0" cellpadding="0" class="t1" style="border-collapse: collapse;">

<tbody>

<tr>

<td valign="top" class="td1" style="border-style: solid; border-width: 1px; border-color: rgb(154, 154, 154); padding: 1px 5px;">

Code

</td>

<td valign="top" class="td1" style="border-style: solid; border-width: 1px; border-color: rgb(154, 154, 154); padding: 1px 5px;">

Keyword

</td>

<td valign="top" class="td1" style="border-style: solid; border-width: 1px; border-color: rgb(154, 154, 154); padding: 1px 5px;">

Description

</td>

</tr>

<tr>

<td valign="top" class="td1" style="border-style: solid; border-width: 1px; border-color: rgb(154, 154, 154); padding: 1px 5px;">

0

</td>

<td valign="top" class="td1" style="border-style: solid; border-width: 1px; border-color: rgb(154, 154, 154); padding: 1px 5px;">

emerg

</td>

<td valign="top" class="td1" style="border-style: solid; border-width: 1px; border-color: rgb(154, 154, 154); padding: 1px 5px;">

The event causes the system to be unusable

</td>

</tr>

<tr>

<td valign="top" class="td1" style="border-style: solid; border-width: 1px; border-color: rgb(154, 154, 154); padding: 1px 5px;">

1

</td>

<td valign="top" class="td1" style="border-style: solid; border-width: 1px; border-color: rgb(154, 154, 154); padding: 1px 5px;">

alert

</td>

<td valign="top" class="td1" style="border-style: solid; border-width: 1px; border-color: rgb(154, 154, 154); padding: 1px 5px;">

An event that requires immediate attention

</td>

</tr>

<tr>

<td valign="top" class="td1" style="border-style: solid; border-width: 1px; border-color: rgb(154, 154, 154); padding: 1px 5px;">

2

</td>

<td valign="top" class="td1" style="border-style: solid; border-width: 1px; border-color: rgb(154, 154, 154); padding: 1px 5px;">

crit

</td>

<td valign="top" class="td1" style="border-style: solid; border-width: 1px; border-color: rgb(154, 154, 154); padding: 1px 5px;">

An event that is critical but doesn’t require immediate attention

</td>

</tr>

<tr>

<td valign="top" class="td1" style="border-style: solid; border-width: 1px; border-color: rgb(154, 154, 154); padding: 1px 5px;">

3

</td>

<td valign="top" class="td1" style="border-style: solid; border-width: 1px; border-color: rgb(154, 154, 154); padding: 1px 5px;">

err

</td>

<td valign="top" class="td1" style="border-style: solid; border-width: 1px; border-color: rgb(154, 154, 154); padding: 1px 5px;">

An error condition that allows the system or application to continue

</td>

</tr>

<tr>

<td valign="top" class="td1" style="border-style: solid; border-width: 1px; border-color: rgb(154, 154, 154); padding: 1px 5px;">

4

</td>

<td valign="top" class="td1" style="border-style: solid; border-width: 1px; border-color: rgb(154, 154, 154); padding: 1px 5px;">

warning

</td>

<td valign="top" class="td1" style="border-style: solid; border-width: 1px; border-color: rgb(154, 154, 154); padding: 1px 5px;">

A non-normal warning condition in the system or application

</td>

</tr>

<tr>

<td valign="top" class="td1" style="border-style: solid; border-width: 1px; border-color: rgb(154, 154, 154); padding: 1px 5px;">

5

</td>

<td valign="top" class="td1" style="border-style: solid; border-width: 1px; border-color: rgb(154, 154, 154); padding: 1px 5px;">

notice

</td>

<td valign="top" class="td1" style="border-style: solid; border-width: 1px; border-color: rgb(154, 154, 154); padding: 1px 5px;">

A normal but significant condition message

</td>

</tr>

<tr>

<td valign="top" class="td1" style="border-style: solid; border-width: 1px; border-color: rgb(154, 154, 154); padding: 1px 5px;">

6

</td>

<td valign="top" class="td1" style="border-style: solid; border-width: 1px; border-color: rgb(154, 154, 154); padding: 1px 5px;">

info

</td>

<td valign="top" class="td1" style="border-style: solid; border-width: 1px; border-color: rgb(154, 154, 154); padding: 1px 5px;">

An informational message from the system

</td>

</tr>

<tr>

<td valign="top" class="td1" style="border-style: solid; border-width: 1px; border-color: rgb(154, 154, 154); padding: 1px 5px;">

7

</td>

<td valign="top" class="td1" style="border-style: solid; border-width: 1px; border-color: rgb(154, 154, 154); padding: 1px 5px;">

debug

</td>

<td valign="top" class="td1" style="border-style: solid; border-width: 1px; border-color: rgb(154, 154, 154); padding: 1px 5px;">

Debugging messages for developers

</td>

</tr>

</tbody>

</table>

- <span class="s1" style="font-variant-numeric: normal; font-variant-east-asian: normal; font-variant-alternates: normal; font-kerning: auto; font-optical-sizing: auto; font-feature-settings: normal; font-variation-settings: normal; font-variant-position: normal; font-stretch: normal; font-size: 12px; line-height: normal;"></span>History of Linux Logging

- <span class="s1" style="font-variant-numeric: normal; font-variant-east-asian: normal; font-variant-alternates: normal; font-kerning: auto; font-optical-sizing: auto; font-feature-settings: normal; font-variation-settings: normal; font-variant-position: normal; font-stretch: normal; font-size: 12px; line-height: normal;"></span>sysklogd —> The original syslog application, it includes two programs: the syslogd program to monitor the system and applications for events, and the klogd program to monitor the Linux kernel for events.
- <span class="s1" style="font-variant-numeric: normal; font-variant-east-asian: normal; font-variant-alternates: normal; font-kerning: auto; font-optical-sizing: auto; font-feature-settings: normal; font-variation-settings: normal; font-variant-position: normal; font-stretch: normal; font-size: 12px; line-height: normal;"></span>syslogd-ng —> Added advanced features, such as message filtering and the ability to send messages to remote hosts.
- <span class="s1" style="font-variant-numeric: normal; font-variant-east-asian: normal; font-variant-alternates: normal; font-kerning: auto; font-optical-sizing: auto; font-feature-settings: normal; font-variation-settings: normal; font-variant-position: normal; font-stretch: normal; font-size: 12px; line-height: normal;"></span>rsyslog —> The project claims the “r” stands for “rocket fast.”Speed is the focus of the rsyslog project, and the rsyslogd application has quickly become the standard logging package for many Linux distributions.
- <span class="s1" style="font-variant-numeric: normal; font-variant-east-asian: normal; font-variant-alternates: normal; font-kerning: auto; font-optical-sizing: auto; font-feature-settings: normal; font-variation-settings: normal; font-variant-position: normal; font-stretch: normal; font-size: 12px; line-height: normal;"></span>systemd-journald —> Part of the systemd application for system startup and initialization, many Linux distributions are now using this for logging. It does not follow the syslog protocol but instead uses a completely different way of reporting and storing system and application events.

rsyslogd

- <span class="s1" style="font-variant-numeric: normal; font-variant-east-asian: normal; font-variant-alternates: normal; font-kerning: auto; font-optical-sizing: auto; font-feature-settings: normal; font-variation-settings: normal; font-variant-position: normal; font-stretch: normal; font-size: 12px; line-height: normal;"></span>/etc/rsyslogd.conf file or \*.conf files in the /etc/rsyslog.d/ directory —> define rules on what events to listen for and how to handle them using The rsyslogd program
- <span class="s1" style="font-variant-numeric: normal; font-variant-east-asian: normal; font-variant-alternates: normal; font-kerning: auto; font-optical-sizing: auto; font-feature-settings: normal; font-variation-settings: normal; font-variant-position: normal; font-stretch: normal; font-size: 12px; line-height: normal;"></span>format of an rsyslogd rule is: facility.priority action

- <span class="s1" style="font-variant-numeric: normal; font-variant-east-asian: normal; font-variant-alternates: normal; font-kerning: auto; font-optical-sizing: auto; font-feature-settings: normal; font-variation-settings: normal; font-variant-position: normal; font-stretch: normal; font-size: 12px; line-height: normal;"></span>The facility entry uses one of the standard syslog protocol facility keywords.
- <span class="s1" style="font-variant-numeric: normal; font-variant-east-asian: normal; font-variant-alternates: normal; font-kerning: auto; font-optical-sizing: auto; font-feature-settings: normal; font-variation-settings: normal; font-variant-position: normal; font-stretch: normal; font-size: 12px; line-height: normal;"></span>The priority entry uses the severity keyword as defined in the syslog protocol, but with a twist.
- <span class="s1" style="font-variant-numeric: normal; font-variant-east-asian: normal; font-variant-alternates: normal; font-kerning: auto; font-optical-sizing: auto; font-feature-settings: normal; font-variation-settings: normal; font-variant-position: normal; font-stretch: normal; font-size: 12px; line-height: normal;"></span>The action entry defines what rsyslogd should do with the received syslog message.

- <span class="s1" style="font-variant-numeric: normal; font-variant-east-asian: normal; font-variant-alternates: normal; font-kerning: auto; font-optical-sizing: auto; font-feature-settings: normal; font-variation-settings: normal; font-variant-position: normal; font-stretch: normal; font-size: 12px; line-height: normal;"></span>Setting Priority

- <span class="s1" style="font-variant-numeric: normal; font-variant-east-asian: normal; font-variant-alternates: normal; font-kerning: auto; font-optical-sizing: auto; font-feature-settings: normal; font-variation-settings: normal; font-variant-position: normal; font-stretch: normal; font-size: 12px; line-height: normal;"></span>kern.crit

- <span class="s1" style="font-variant-numeric: normal; font-variant-east-asian: normal; font-variant-alternates: normal; font-kerning: auto; font-optical-sizing: auto; font-feature-settings: normal; font-variation-settings: normal; font-variant-position: normal; font-stretch: normal; font-size: 12px; line-height: normal;"></span>logs all kernel event messages with a severity of ritical, alert, or emergency.
- <span class="s1" style="font-variant-numeric: normal; font-variant-east-asian: normal; font-variant-alternates: normal; font-kerning: auto; font-optical-sizing: auto; font-feature-settings: normal; font-variation-settings: normal; font-variant-position: normal; font-stretch: normal; font-size: 12px; line-height: normal;"></span>When you define a severity, syslogd will log all events with that severity or higher (lower severity code).

- <span class="s1" style="font-variant-numeric: normal; font-variant-east-asian: normal; font-variant-alternates: normal; font-kerning: auto; font-optical-sizing: auto; font-feature-settings: normal; font-variation-settings: normal; font-variant-position: normal; font-stretch: normal; font-size: 12px; line-height: normal;"></span>kern.=crit

- <span class="s1" style="font-variant-numeric: normal; font-variant-east-asian: normal; font-variant-alternates: normal; font-kerning: auto; font-optical-sizing: auto; font-feature-settings: normal; font-variation-settings: normal; font-variant-position: normal; font-stretch: normal; font-size: 12px; line-height: normal;"></span>logs only messages with a specific severity

- <span class="s1" style="font-variant-numeric: normal; font-variant-east-asian: normal; font-variant-alternates: normal; font-kerning: auto; font-optical-sizing: auto; font-feature-settings: normal; font-variation-settings: normal; font-variant-position: normal; font-stretch: normal; font-size: 12px; line-height: normal;"></span>\*.emerg

- <span class="s1" style="font-variant-numeric: normal; font-variant-east-asian: normal; font-variant-alternates: normal; font-kerning: auto; font-optical-sizing: auto; font-feature-settings: normal; font-variation-settings: normal; font-variant-position: normal; font-stretch: normal; font-size: 12px; line-height: normal;"></span>logs all events with an emergency severity level use wildcard characters for either the facility or priority.

- <span class="s1" style="font-variant-numeric: normal; font-variant-east-asian: normal; font-variant-alternates: normal; font-kerning: auto; font-optical-sizing: auto; font-feature-settings: normal; font-variation-settings: normal; font-variant-position: normal; font-stretch: normal; font-size: 12px; line-height: normal;"></span>Actions

- Forward to a regular file
- Pipe the message to an application
- Display the message on a terminal or the system console
- Send the message to a remote host
- Send the message to a list of users
- Send the message to all logged-in users

- <span class="s1" style="font-variant-numeric: normal; font-variant-east-asian: normal; font-variant-alternates: normal; font-kerning: auto; font-optical-sizing: auto; font-feature-settings: normal; font-variation-settings: normal; font-variant-position: normal; font-stretch: normal; font-size: 12px; line-height: normal;"></span>rsyslogd.conf configuration entries, for Ubuntu 18.04:<span class="Apple-converted-space"> </span>

- <span class="s1" style="font-variant-numeric: normal; font-variant-east-asian: normal; font-variant-alternates: normal; font-kerning: auto; font-optical-sizing: auto; font-feature-settings: normal; font-variation-settings: normal; font-variant-position: normal; font-stretch: normal; font-size: 12px; line-height: normal;"></span>auth,authpriv.\* /var/log/auth.log
- <span class="s1" style="font-variant-numeric: normal; font-variant-east-asian: normal; font-variant-alternates: normal; font-kerning: auto; font-optical-sizing: auto; font-feature-settings: normal; font-variation-settings: normal; font-variant-position: normal; font-stretch: normal; font-size: 12px; line-height: normal;"></span>_._;auth,authpriv.none -/var/log/syslog
- <span class="s1" style="font-variant-numeric: normal; font-variant-east-asian: normal; font-variant-alternates: normal; font-kerning: auto; font-optical-sizing: auto; font-feature-settings: normal; font-variation-settings: normal; font-variant-position: normal; font-stretch: normal; font-size: 12px; line-height: normal;"></span>kern.\* -/var/log/kern.log
- <span class="s1" style="font-variant-numeric: normal; font-variant-east-asian: normal; font-variant-alternates: normal; font-kerning: auto; font-optical-sizing: auto; font-feature-settings: normal; font-variation-settings: normal; font-variant-position: normal; font-stretch: normal; font-size: 12px; line-height: normal;"></span>mail.\* -/var/log/mail.log
- <span class="s1" style="font-variant-numeric: normal; font-variant-east-asian: normal; font-variant-alternates: normal; font-kerning: auto; font-optical-sizing: auto; font-feature-settings: normal; font-variation-settings: normal; font-variant-position: normal; font-stretch: normal; font-size: 12px; line-height: normal;"></span>mail.err /var/log/mail.err
- <span class="s1" style="font-variant-numeric: normal; font-variant-east-asian: normal; font-variant-alternates: normal; font-kerning: auto; font-optical-sizing: auto; font-feature-settings: normal; font-variation-settings: normal; font-variant-position: normal; font-stretch: normal; font-size: 12px; line-height: normal;"></span>_.emerg :omusrmsg:_

- <span class="s1" style="font-variant-numeric: normal; font-variant-east-asian: normal; font-variant-alternates: normal; font-kerning: auto; font-optical-sizing: auto; font-feature-settings: normal; font-variation-settings: normal; font-variant-position: normal; font-stretch: normal; font-size: 12px; line-height: normal;"></span>rsyslogd.conf configuration entries, for CentOS 7:

- <span class="s1" style="font-variant-numeric: normal; font-variant-east-asian: normal; font-variant-alternates: normal; font-kerning: auto; font-optical-sizing: auto; font-feature-settings: normal; font-variation-settings: normal; font-variant-position: normal; font-stretch: normal; font-size: 12px; line-height: normal;"></span>\*.info;mail.none;authpriv.none;cron.none /var/log/messages
- <span class="s1" style="font-variant-numeric: normal; font-variant-east-asian: normal; font-variant-alternates: normal; font-kerning: auto; font-optical-sizing: auto; font-feature-settings: normal; font-variation-settings: normal; font-variant-position: normal; font-stretch: normal; font-size: 12px; line-height: normal;"></span>authpriv.\* /var/log/secure
- <span class="s1" style="font-variant-numeric: normal; font-variant-east-asian: normal; font-variant-alternates: normal; font-kerning: auto; font-optical-sizing: auto; font-feature-settings: normal; font-variation-settings: normal; font-variant-position: normal; font-stretch: normal; font-size: 12px; line-height: normal;"></span>mail.\* -/var/log/maillog
- <span class="s1" style="font-variant-numeric: normal; font-variant-east-asian: normal; font-variant-alternates: normal; font-kerning: auto; font-optical-sizing: auto; font-feature-settings: normal; font-variation-settings: normal; font-variant-position: normal; font-stretch: normal; font-size: 12px; line-height: normal;"></span>cron.\* /var/log/cron
- <span class="s1" style="font-variant-numeric: normal; font-variant-east-asian: normal; font-variant-alternates: normal; font-kerning: auto; font-optical-sizing: auto; font-feature-settings: normal; font-variation-settings: normal; font-variant-position: normal; font-stretch: normal; font-size: 12px; line-height: normal;"></span>_.emerg :omusrmsg:_
- <span class="s1" style="font-variant-numeric: normal; font-variant-east-asian: normal; font-variant-alternates: normal; font-kerning: auto; font-optical-sizing: auto; font-feature-settings: normal; font-variation-settings: normal; font-variant-position: normal; font-stretch: normal; font-size: 12px; line-height: normal;"></span>uucp,news.crit /var/log/spooler
- <span class="s1" style="font-variant-numeric: normal; font-variant-east-asian: normal; font-variant-alternates: normal; font-kerning: auto; font-optical-sizing: auto; font-feature-settings: normal; font-variation-settings: normal; font-variant-position: normal; font-stretch: normal; font-size: 12px; line-height: normal;"></span>local7.\* /var/log/boot.log

- <span class="s1" style="font-variant-numeric: normal; font-variant-east-asian: normal; font-variant-alternates: normal; font-kerning: auto; font-optical-sizing: auto; font-feature-settings: normal; font-variation-settings: normal; font-variant-position: normal; font-stretch: normal; font-size: 12px; line-height: normal;"></span>A common server these days in many data centers is a central logging host that receives and stores logs for all its various log client systems. Configuring your system to act as a logging client is fairly easy using the rsyslog application’s configuration file(s). for doing so, edit the /etc/rsyslogd.conf configuration file and go to the file’s bottom:<span class="Apple-converted-space"> </span>
- <span class="s1" style="font-variant-numeric: normal; font-variant-east-asian: normal; font-variant-alternates: normal; font-kerning: auto; font-optical-sizing: auto; font-feature-settings: normal; font-variation-settings: normal; font-variant-position: normal; font-stretch: normal; font-size: 12px; line-height: normal;"></span>TCP|UDP[(z#)]HOST:[PORT#Linux —> _._ @@(z9)[loghost.anisa.co.ir:6514](http://loghost.anisa.co.ir:6514)

- <span class="s1" style="font-variant-numeric: normal; font-variant-east-asian: normal; font-variant-alternates: normal; font-kerning: auto; font-optical-sizing: auto; font-feature-settings: normal; font-variation-settings: normal; font-variant-position: normal; font-stretch: normal; font-size: 12px; line-height: normal;"></span>TCP|UDP: You can select either the TCP or UDP protocols to transport your log messages to the central log server. UDP can lose data, so you should select TCP if your log messages are important. Use a single at sign (@) to select UDP and double at signs (@@) to choose TCP.
- <span class="s1" style="font-variant-numeric: normal; font-variant-east-asian: normal; font-variant-alternates: normal; font-kerning: auto; font-optical-sizing: auto; font-feature-settings: normal; font-variation-settings: normal; font-variant-position: normal; font-stretch: normal; font-size: 12px; line-height: normal;"></span>[(z#)]: this syntax is optional. The z selects zlib to compress the data prior to traversing the network, and the # picks the compression level, which can be any number between 1 (lowest compression) and 9 (highest compression).
- <span class="s1" style="font-variant-numeric: normal; font-variant-east-asian: normal; font-variant-alternates: normal; font-kerning: auto; font-optical-sizing: auto; font-feature-settings: normal; font-variation-settings: normal; font-variant-position: normal; font-stretch: normal; font-size: 12px; line-height: normal;"></span>HOST: designates the central logging server either by a fully qualified domain name (FQDN), such as example.com, or an IP address. If you use an IPv6 address, it must be encased in brackets.
- <span class="s1" style="font-variant-numeric: normal; font-variant-east-asian: normal; font-variant-alternates: normal; font-kerning: auto; font-optical-sizing: auto; font-feature-settings: normal; font-variation-settings: normal; font-variant-position: normal; font-stretch: normal; font-size: 12px; line-height: normal;"></span>[PORT#]: this syntax is optional. designates the port on the remote central logging host where the log service is listening for incoming traffic.

logrotate

- <span class="s1" style="font-variant-numeric: normal; font-variant-east-asian: normal; font-variant-alternates: normal; font-kerning: auto; font-optical-sizing: auto; font-feature-settings: normal; font-variation-settings: normal; font-variant-position: normal; font-stretch: normal; font-size: 12px; line-height: normal;"></span>For busy Linux systems it doesn’t take long to generate large log files. so many Linux distributions install the logrotate utility. It automatically splits rsyslogdlog files into archive files based on a time or the size of the file. You can usually identify archived log files by a numerical extension added to the log filename.
- <span class="s1" style="font-variant-numeric: normal; font-variant-east-asian: normal; font-variant-alternates: normal; font-kerning: auto; font-optical-sizing: auto; font-feature-settings: normal; font-variation-settings: normal; font-variant-position: normal; font-stretch: normal; font-size: 12px; line-height: normal;"></span>logrotate can also compress, delete, and if desired, mail a log file to a designated account.
- <span class="s1" style="font-variant-numeric: normal; font-variant-east-asian: normal; font-variant-alternates: normal; font-kerning: auto; font-optical-sizing: auto; font-feature-settings: normal; font-variation-settings: normal; font-variant-position: normal; font-stretch: normal; font-size: 12px; line-height: normal;"></span>To ensure the files are handled in a timely manner, the logrotate utility is typically run every day as a cron job.
- <span class="s1" style="font-variant-numeric: normal; font-variant-east-asian: normal; font-variant-alternates: normal; font-kerning: auto; font-optical-sizing: auto; font-feature-settings: normal; font-variation-settings: normal; font-variant-position: normal; font-stretch: normal; font-size: 12px; line-height: normal;"></span>/etc/logrotate.conf —> configuration file to determine how each log file is managed.

- <span class="s1" style="font-variant-numeric: normal; font-variant-east-asian: normal; font-variant-alternates: normal; font-kerning: auto; font-optical-sizing: auto; font-feature-settings: normal; font-variation-settings: normal; font-variant-position: normal; font-stretch: normal; font-size: 12px; line-height: normal;"></span>$ logger —> enter messages into the system log. If you create and run scripts on your Linux system, you may want to log your own application events.

- <span class="s1" style="font-variant-numeric: normal; font-variant-east-asian: normal; font-variant-alternates: normal; font-kerning: auto; font-optical-sizing: auto; font-feature-settings: normal; font-variation-settings: normal; font-variant-position: normal; font-stretch: normal; font-size: 12px; line-height: normal;"></span>most Linux distributions create log files in the /var/log directory.
- <span class="s1" style="font-variant-numeric: normal; font-variant-east-asian: normal; font-variant-alternates: normal; font-kerning: auto; font-optical-sizing: auto; font-feature-settings: normal; font-variation-settings: normal; font-variant-position: normal; font-stretch: normal; font-size: 12px; line-height: normal;"></span>Depending on the security of the Linux system, many log files are readable by everyone, but some may not be.
- <span class="s1" style="font-variant-numeric: normal; font-variant-east-asian: normal; font-variant-alternates: normal; font-kerning: auto; font-optical-sizing: auto; font-feature-settings: normal; font-variation-settings: normal; font-variant-position: normal; font-stretch: normal; font-size: 12px; line-height: normal;"></span>It’s also common for individual applications to have a separate directory under the /var/log directory for their own application event messages, such as /var/log/apache2 for the Apache web server.
- <span class="s1" style="font-variant-numeric: normal; font-variant-east-asian: normal; font-variant-alternates: normal; font-kerning: auto; font-optical-sizing: auto; font-feature-settings: normal; font-variation-settings: normal; font-variant-position: normal; font-stretch: normal; font-size: 12px; line-height: normal;"></span>Since rsyslogd log files are text files, you can use any of the standard text tools available in Linux, such as cat, head, tail, as well as filtering tools, such as grep, to view the files and search them. One common trick for administrators is to watch a log file by using the -f option with the tail command. That displays the last few lines in the log file but then monitors the file for any new entries and displays those too.

systemd-journald

- <span class="s1" style="font-variant-numeric: normal; font-variant-east-asian: normal; font-variant-alternates: normal; font-kerning: auto; font-optical-sizing: auto; font-feature-settings: normal; font-variation-settings: normal; font-variant-position: normal; font-stretch: normal; font-size: 12px; line-height: normal;"></span>we call it a journal utility instead of a logging utility
- <span class="s1" style="font-variant-numeric: normal; font-variant-east-asian: normal; font-variant-alternates: normal; font-kerning: auto; font-optical-sizing: auto; font-feature-settings: normal; font-variation-settings: normal; font-variant-position: normal; font-stretch: normal; font-size: 12px; line-height: normal;"></span>The system-journald program uses a completely different method of storing event messages from the syslog protocol. However, it does store syslog messages as well as notes from the kernel, boot events, service messages, and so on.
- <span class="s1" style="font-variant-numeric: normal; font-variant-east-asian: normal; font-variant-alternates: normal; font-kerning: auto; font-optical-sizing: auto; font-feature-settings: normal; font-variation-settings: normal; font-variant-position: normal; font-stretch: normal; font-size: 12px; line-height: normal;"></span>/etc/systemd/journald.conf —> The systemd-journald service reads its configuration from this configuration file.

<table cellspacing="0" cellpadding="0" class="t1" style="border-collapse: collapse;">

<tbody>

<tr>

<td valign="top" class="td1" style="border-style: solid; border-width: 1px; border-color: rgb(154, 154, 154); padding: 1px 5px;">

Directive

</td>

<td valign="top" class="td1" style="border-style: solid; border-width: 1px; border-color: rgb(154, 154, 154); padding: 1px 5px;">

Description

</td>

</tr>

<tr>

<td valign="top" class="td1" style="border-style: solid; border-width: 1px; border-color: rgb(154, 154, 154); padding: 1px 5px;">

Storage=

</td>

<td valign="top" class="td1" style="border-style: solid; border-width: 1px; border-color: rgb(154, 154, 154); padding: 1px 5px;">

Set to auto, persistent, volatile, or none. Determines how systemd-journald stores event messages. (Default is auto.)

</td>

</tr>

<tr>

<td valign="top" class="td1" style="border-style: solid; border-width: 1px; border-color: rgb(154, 154, 154); padding: 1px 5px;">

Compress=

</td>

<td valign="top" class="td1" style="border-style: solid; border-width: 1px; border-color: rgb(154, 154, 154); padding: 1px 5px;">

Set to yes or no. If yes, journal files are compressed. (Default is yes.)

</td>

</tr>

<tr>

<td valign="top" class="td1" style="border-style: solid; border-width: 1px; border-color: rgb(154, 154, 154); padding: 1px 5px;">

ForwardToSyslog=

</td>

<td valign="top" class="td1" style="border-style: solid; border-width: 1px; border-color: rgb(154, 154, 154); padding: 1px 5px;">

Set to yes or no. If yes, any received messages are forwarded to a separate syslog program, such as rsyslogd, running on the system. (Default is yes.)

</td>

</tr>

<tr>

<td valign="top" class="td1" style="border-style: solid; border-width: 1px; border-color: rgb(154, 154, 154); padding: 1px 5px;">

ForwardToWall=

</td>

<td valign="top" class="td1" style="border-style: solid; border-width: 1px; border-color: rgb(154, 154, 154); padding: 1px 5px;">

Set to yes or no. If yes, any received messages are forwarded as wall messages to all users currently logged into the system. (Default is yes.)

</td>

</tr>

<tr>

<td valign="top" class="td1" style="border-style: solid; border-width: 1px; border-color: rgb(154, 154, 154); padding: 1px 5px;">

MaxFileSec=

</td>

<td valign="top" class="td1" style="border-style: solid; border-width: 1px; border-color: rgb(154, 154, 154); padding: 1px 5px;">

Set to a number followed by a time unit (such as month, week, or day) that sets the amount of time before a journal file is rotated (archived). Typically this is not needed if a size limitation is employed. To turn this feature off, set the number to 0 with no time unit. (Default is 1month.)

</td>

</tr>

<tr>

<td valign="top" class="td1" style="border-style: solid; border-width: 1px; border-color: rgb(154, 154, 154); padding: 1px 5px;">

RuntimeKeepFree=<span class="Apple-converted-space"> </span>

</td>

<td valign="top" class="td1" style="border-style: solid; border-width: 1px; border-color: rgb(154, 154, 154); padding: 1px 5px;">

Set to a number followed by a unit (such as K, M, or G) that sets the amount of disk space systemd-journald must keep free for other disk usages when employing volatile storage. (Default is 15% of current space.)

</td>

</tr>

<tr>

<td valign="top" class="td1" style="border-style: solid; border-width: 1px; border-color: rgb(154, 154, 154); padding: 1px 5px;">

RuntimeMaxFileSize=

</td>

<td valign="top" class="td1" style="border-style: solid; border-width: 1px; border-color: rgb(154, 154, 154); padding: 1px 5px;">

Set to a number followed by a unit (such as K, M, or G) that sets the amount of disk space systemd-journald journal files can consume if it is volatile.

</td>

</tr>

<tr>

<td valign="top" class="td1" style="border-style: solid; border-width: 1px; border-color: rgb(154, 154, 154); padding: 1px 5px;">

RuntimeMaxUse=

</td>

<td valign="top" class="td1" style="border-style: solid; border-width: 1px; border-color: rgb(154, 154, 154); padding: 1px 5px;">

Set to a number followed by a unit (such as K, M, or G) that sets the amount of disk space systemd-journald can consume when employing volatile storage. (Default is 10% of current space.)

</td>

</tr>

<tr>

<td valign="top" class="td1" style="border-style: solid; border-width: 1px; border-color: rgb(154, 154, 154); padding: 1px 5px;">

SystemKeepFree=

</td>

<td valign="top" class="td1" style="border-style: solid; border-width: 1px; border-color: rgb(154, 154, 154); padding: 1px 5px;">

Set to a number followed by a unit (such as K, M, or G) that sets the amount of disk space systemd-journald must keep free for other disk usages when employing persistent storage. (Default is 15% of current space.)

</td>

</tr>

<tr>

<td valign="top" class="td1" style="border-style: solid; border-width: 1px; border-color: rgb(154, 154, 154); padding: 1px 5px;">

SystemMaxFileSize=

</td>

<td valign="top" class="td1" style="border-style: solid; border-width: 1px; border-color: rgb(154, 154, 154); padding: 1px 5px;">

Set to a number followed by a unit (such as K, M, or G) that sets the amount of disk space systemd-journald journal files can consume if it is persistent.

</td>

</tr>

<tr>

<td valign="top" class="td1" style="border-style: solid; border-width: 1px; border-color: rgb(154, 154, 154); padding: 1px 5px;">

SystemMaxUse=

</td>

<td valign="top" class="td1" style="border-style: solid; border-width: 1px; border-color: rgb(154, 154, 154); padding: 1px 5px;">

Set to a number followed by a unit (such as K, M, or G) that sets the amount of disk space systemd-journald can consume when

employing persistent storage. (Default is 10% of current space.)

</td>

</tr>

</tbody>

</table>

- <span class="s1" style="font-variant-numeric: normal; font-variant-east-asian: normal; font-variant-alternates: normal; font-kerning: auto; font-optical-sizing: auto; font-feature-settings: normal; font-variation-settings: normal; font-variant-position: normal; font-stretch: normal; font-size: 12px; line-height: normal;"></span>Storage Directive Values

- <span class="s1" style="font-variant-numeric: normal; font-variant-east-asian: normal; font-variant-alternates: normal; font-kerning: auto; font-optical-sizing: auto; font-feature-settings: normal; font-variation-settings: normal; font-variant-position: normal; font-stretch: normal; font-size: 12px; line-height: normal;"></span>auto: Causes systemd-journald to look for the /var/log/journal directory and store event messages there. If that directory doesn’t exist, it stores the event messages in the temporary /run/log/journal directory, which is deleted when the system shuts down.
- <span class="s1" style="font-variant-numeric: normal; font-variant-east-asian: normal; font-variant-alternates: normal; font-kerning: auto; font-optical-sizing: auto; font-feature-settings: normal; font-variation-settings: normal; font-variant-position: normal; font-stretch: normal; font-size: 12px; line-height: normal;"></span>persistent: Causes systemd-journald to automatically create the /var/log/journal directory if it doesn’t currently exist and store event messages there.
- <span class="s1" style="font-variant-numeric: normal; font-variant-east-asian: normal; font-variant-alternates: normal; font-kerning: auto; font-optical-sizing: auto; font-feature-settings: normal; font-variation-settings: normal; font-variant-position: normal; font-stretch: normal; font-size: 12px; line-height: normal;"></span>volatile: Forces systemd-journald to store only event messages in the temporary /run/log/journal directory.
- <span class="s1" style="font-variant-numeric: normal; font-variant-east-asian: normal; font-variant-alternates: normal; font-kerning: auto; font-optical-sizing: auto; font-feature-settings: normal; font-variation-settings: normal; font-variant-position: normal; font-stretch: normal; font-size: 12px; line-height: normal;"></span>none: Event messages are discarded.

- <span class="s1" style="font-variant-numeric: normal; font-variant-east-asian: normal; font-variant-alternates: normal; font-kerning: auto; font-optical-sizing: auto; font-feature-settings: normal; font-variation-settings: normal; font-variant-position: normal; font-stretch: normal; font-size: 12px; line-height: normal;"></span>You may have one or more active journal files on your system, depending on how systemd-journald is configured. For example, if you have Storage set to persistent, you can employ the SplitMode directive to divide up the journal file into multiple active files, one per user as well as a system journal file.
- <span class="s1" style="font-variant-numeric: normal; font-variant-east-asian: normal; font-variant-alternates: normal; font-kerning: auto; font-optical-sizing: auto; font-feature-settings: normal; font-variation-settings: normal; font-variant-position: normal; font-stretch: normal; font-size: 12px; line-height: normal;"></span>the system’s active journal file is named system.journal, with user active journal files (if used) named user-UID.journal.
- <span class="s1" style="font-variant-numeric: normal; font-variant-east-asian: normal; font-variant-alternates: normal; font-kerning: auto; font-optical-sizing: auto; font-feature-settings: normal; font-variation-settings: normal; font-variant-position: normal; font-stretch: normal; font-size: 12px; line-height: normal;"></span>After the files are rotated, they are renamed and considered archived. The archived journal filenames start with either system or user-UID, contain an @ followed by several letters and numbers, and end in a .journalfile extension.
- <span class="s1" style="font-variant-numeric: normal; font-variant-east-asian: normal; font-variant-alternates: normal; font-kerning: auto; font-optical-sizing: auto; font-feature-settings: normal; font-variation-settings: normal; font-variant-position: normal; font-stretch: normal; font-size: 12px; line-height: normal;"></span>you can have both systemd-journald and a syslog protocol application, such as rsyslog, running and working together.
- <span class="s1" style="font-variant-numeric: normal; font-variant-east-asian: normal; font-variant-alternates: normal; font-kerning: auto; font-optical-sizing: auto; font-feature-settings: normal; font-variation-settings: normal; font-variant-position: normal; font-stretch: normal; font-size: 12px; line-height: normal;"></span>There are two primary ways to accomplish this:

- <span class="s1" style="font-variant-numeric: normal; font-variant-east-asian: normal; font-variant-alternates: normal; font-kerning: auto; font-optical-sizing: auto; font-feature-settings: normal; font-variation-settings: normal; font-variant-position: normal; font-stretch: normal; font-size: 12px; line-height: normal;"></span>Journal Client Method: allows a syslog protocol program to act as a journal client, reading entries stored in the journal file(s). It is the preferred way, because it avoids losing any important messages that may occur during the system boot, before the syslog service starts.
- <span class="s1" style="font-variant-numeric: normal; font-variant-east-asian: normal; font-variant-alternates: normal; font-kerning: auto; font-optical-sizing: auto; font-feature-settings: normal; font-variation-settings: normal; font-variant-position: normal; font-stretch: normal; font-size: 12px; line-height: normal;"></span>Forward to Syslog Method: employs the file /run/systemd/journal/syslog. Messages are forwarded to the file (called a socket) where a syslog protocol program can read them.

- <span class="s1" style="font-variant-numeric: normal; font-variant-east-asian: normal; font-variant-alternates: normal; font-kerning: auto; font-optical-sizing: auto; font-feature-settings: normal; font-variation-settings: normal; font-variant-position: normal; font-stretch: normal; font-size: 12px; line-height: normal;"></span>systemd-journald program does not store journal entries in text format, they are binary format and work similar to a DB
- <span class="s1" style="font-variant-numeric: normal; font-variant-east-asian: normal; font-variant-alternates: normal; font-kerning: auto; font-optical-sizing: auto; font-feature-settings: normal; font-variation-settings: normal; font-variant-position: normal; font-stretch: normal; font-size: 12px; line-height: normal;"></span>$ journalctl —> query the systemd journal
- <span class="s1" style="font-variant-numeric: normal; font-variant-east-asian: normal; font-variant-alternates: normal; font-kerning: auto; font-optical-sizing: auto; font-feature-settings: normal; font-variation-settings: normal; font-variant-position: normal; font-stretch: normal; font-size: 12px; line-height: normal;"></span>Common journalctl MATCHES Parameter Used For Filtering

- <span class="s1" style="font-variant-numeric: normal; font-variant-east-asian: normal; font-variant-alternates: normal; font-kerning: auto; font-optical-sizing: auto; font-feature-settings: normal; font-variation-settings: normal; font-variant-position: normal; font-stretch: normal; font-size: 12px; line-height: normal;"></span>field —> Match the specific field in the journal. Can enter multiple occurrences of field on same line but must be separated with a space. You can separate multiple field specifications with a plus sign (+) to use a logical or between them.
- <span class="s1" style="font-variant-numeric: normal; font-variant-east-asian: normal; font-variant-alternates: normal; font-kerning: auto; font-optical-sizing: auto; font-feature-settings: normal; font-variation-settings: normal; font-variant-position: normal; font-stretch: normal; font-size: 12px; line-height: normal;"></span>OBJECT_PID=pid —> Match only entries made by the specified application pid.
- <span class="s1" style="font-variant-numeric: normal; font-variant-east-asian: normal; font-variant-alternates: normal; font-kerning: auto; font-optical-sizing: auto; font-feature-settings: normal; font-variation-settings: normal; font-variant-position: normal; font-stretch: normal; font-size: 12px; line-height: normal;"></span>PRIORITY=value —> Match only entries with the specified priority value. The value can be set to one of the following numbers or keywords: emerg (0), alert (1), crit (2), err (3), warning (4), notice (5), info (6), debug (7).
- <span class="s1" style="font-variant-numeric: normal; font-variant-east-asian: normal; font-variant-alternates: normal; font-kerning: auto; font-optical-sizing: auto; font-feature-settings: normal; font-variation-settings: normal; font-variant-position: normal; font-stretch: normal; font-size: 12px; line-height: normal;"></span>\_HOSTNAME=host —> Match only entries from the specified host.
- <span class="s1" style="font-variant-numeric: normal; font-variant-east-asian: normal; font-variant-alternates: normal; font-kerning: auto; font-optical-sizing: auto; font-feature-settings: normal; font-variation-settings: normal; font-variant-position: normal; font-stretch: normal; font-size: 12px; line-height: normal;"></span>\_SYSTEMD_UNIT=unit.type —> Match only entries made by the specified systemd unit. type.
- <span class="s1" style="font-variant-numeric: normal; font-variant-east-asian: normal; font-variant-alternates: normal; font-kerning: auto; font-optical-sizing: auto; font-feature-settings: normal; font-variation-settings: normal; font-variant-position: normal; font-stretch: normal; font-size: 12px; line-height: normal;"></span>\_TRANSPORT=transport —> Match only entries received by the specified transport method.
- <span class="s1" style="font-variant-numeric: normal; font-variant-east-asian: normal; font-variant-alternates: normal; font-kerning: auto; font-optical-sizing: auto; font-feature-settings: normal; font-variation-settings: normal; font-variant-position: normal; font-stretch: normal; font-size: 12px; line-height: normal;"></span>\_UDEV_SYSNAME=dev —> Match only entries received from the specified device.
- <span class="s1" style="font-variant-numeric: normal; font-variant-east-asian: normal; font-variant-alternates: normal; font-kerning: auto; font-optical-sizing: auto; font-feature-settings: normal; font-variation-settings: normal; font-variant-position: normal; font-stretch: normal; font-size: 12px; line-height: normal;"></span>\_UID=userid —> Match only entries made by the specified user ID.

- <span class="s1" style="font-variant-numeric: normal; font-variant-east-asian: normal; font-variant-alternates: normal; font-kerning: auto; font-optical-sizing: auto; font-feature-settings: normal; font-variation-settings: normal; font-variant-position: normal; font-stretch: normal; font-size: 12px; line-height: normal;"></span>$ journalctl --disk-usage —> check the current disk usage of the journal file(s) by employing the command.
- <span class="s1" style="font-variant-numeric: normal; font-variant-east-asian: normal; font-variant-alternates: normal; font-kerning: auto; font-optical-sizing: auto; font-feature-settings: normal; font-variation-settings: normal; font-variant-position: normal; font-stretch: normal; font-size: 12px; line-height: normal;"></span>$ journalctl --vacuum-size —> manually clean up disk space by size (K,M,G or T)
- <span class="s1" style="font-variant-numeric: normal; font-variant-east-asian: normal; font-variant-alternates: normal; font-kerning: auto; font-optical-sizing: auto; font-feature-settings: normal; font-variation-settings: normal; font-variant-position: normal; font-stretch: normal; font-size: 12px; line-height: normal;"></span>$ journalctl --vacuum-size —> manually clean up disk space by time (s, min, h, days, mont

<span class="Apple-converted-space"> </span>(vacuum options work only on archived journal files.)

- <span class="s1" style="font-variant-numeric: normal; font-variant-east-asian: normal; font-variant-alternates: normal; font-kerning: auto; font-optical-sizing: auto; font-feature-settings: normal; font-variation-settings: normal; font-variant-position: normal; font-stretch: normal; font-size: 12px; line-height: normal;"></span>-D directory-name, --directory=directory-name —> Because journalctl looks for the active journal files in either the /run/log/journal or the /var/log/journal directory, you can point it to a different directory location where a copied or another system’s journal file is located
- <span class="s1" style="font-variant-numeric: normal; font-variant-east-asian: normal; font-variant-alternates: normal; font-kerning: auto; font-optical-sizing: auto; font-feature-settings: normal; font-variation-settings: normal; font-variant-position: normal; font-stretch: normal; font-size: 12px; line-height: normal;"></span>--file=pattern —> If the file you are trying to view has a different name than system.journal or user-UID.journal. Set the pattern to be the exact name of the file you wish to view.
- <span class="s1" style="font-variant-numeric: normal; font-variant-east-asian: normal; font-variant-alternates: normal; font-kerning: auto; font-optical-sizing: auto; font-feature-settings: normal; font-variation-settings: normal; font-variant-position: normal; font-stretch: normal; font-size: 12px; line-height: normal;"></span>-m or --merge —> If you have recently rescued your system and now have two or more journal files with entries to view, you can merge them. Keep in mind this does not physically merge the journal files but instead merges their entries in the output for your perusal.
- <span class="s1" style="font-variant-numeric: normal; font-variant-east-asian: normal; font-variant-alternates: normal; font-kerning: auto; font-optical-sizing: auto; font-feature-settings: normal; font-variation-settings: normal; font-variant-position: normal; font-stretch: normal; font-size: 12px; line-height: normal;"></span>$ systemd-cat —> Connect a pipeline or program's output with the journal.

- <span class="s1" style="font-variant-numeric: normal; font-variant-east-asian: normal; font-variant-alternates: normal; font-kerning: auto; font-optical-sizing: auto; font-feature-settings: normal; font-variation-settings: normal; font-variant-position: normal; font-stretch: normal; font-size: 12px; line-height: normal;"></span>$ echo "Test of systemd-cat" | systemd-cat

———————————————

**Network:**

- <span class="s1" style="font-variant-numeric: normal; font-variant-east-asian: normal; font-variant-alternates: normal; font-kerning: auto; font-optical-sizing: auto; font-feature-settings: normal; font-variation-settings: normal; font-variant-position: normal; font-stretch: normal; font-size: 12px; line-height: normal;"></span>OSI (Open Systems Interconnection) Model:

1.  Physical Lyaer: the hardware required to connect your Linux system to the network: wired - wireless

- <span class="s1" style="font-variant-numeric: normal; font-variant-east-asian: normal; font-variant-alternates: normal; font-kerning: auto; font-optical-sizing: auto; font-feature-settings: normal; font-variation-settings: normal; font-variant-position: normal; font-stretch: normal; font-size: 12px; line-height: normal;"></span>Each access point uses a unique service set identifier (SSID) to identify it from other access points. You just tell your Linux system which access point to connect to by specifying the correct SSID value

3.  Network layer: controls how data is sent between connected network devices, both in your local network and across the Internet.<span class="Apple-converted-space"> </span> For data to get to the correct destination device, some type of network addressing scheme must be used to uniquely identify each network device.

- <span class="s1" style="font-variant-numeric: normal; font-variant-east-asian: normal; font-variant-alternates: normal; font-kerning: auto; font-optical-sizing: auto; font-feature-settings: normal; font-variation-settings: normal; font-variant-position: normal; font-stretch: normal; font-size: 12px; line-height: normal;"></span>IP address: a unique 32-bit address.<span class="Apple-converted-space"> </span> Network layer embeds the source and destination IP addresses into the data packet. To make it easier for humans to recognize the address, IP addresses are split intovfour 8-bit values, represented by decimal numbers, with a period between each value. Format is called dotted-decimal notation. IP addresses are split into two sections:

- <span class="s1" style="font-variant-numeric: normal; font-variant-east-asian: normal; font-variant-alternates: normal; font-kerning: auto; font-optical-sizing: auto; font-feature-settings: normal; font-variation-settings: normal; font-variant-position: normal; font-stretch: normal; font-size: 12px; line-height: normal;"></span>the network address: All devices on the same physical network have the same network address portion of their IP addresses.
- <span class="s1" style="font-variant-numeric: normal; font-variant-east-asian: normal; font-variant-alternates: normal; font-kerning: auto; font-optical-sizing: auto; font-feature-settings: normal; font-variation-settings: normal; font-variant-position: normal; font-stretch: normal; font-size: 12px; line-height: normal;"></span>the host address: Each device on the same network must have a unique host address.

- <span class="s1" style="font-variant-numeric: normal; font-variant-east-asian: normal; font-variant-alternates: normal; font-kerning: auto; font-optical-sizing: auto; font-feature-settings: normal; font-variation-settings: normal; font-variant-position: normal; font-stretch: normal; font-size: 12px; line-height: normal;"></span>Netmask value: distinguishes between the network and host address portions in the IP address by using 1 bit to show which bits of the 32-bit IP address are used by the network and 0 bits to show which bits represent the host address. most people don’t like working with binary numbers, the netmask address is usually shown in dotted-decimal format. For example, the netmask address 255.255.255.0 indicates the first three decimal numbers in the IP address represent the network address, and the last decimal number represents the host address. \

- <span class="s1" style="font-variant-numeric: normal; font-variant-east-asian: normal; font-variant-alternates: normal; font-kerning: auto; font-optical-sizing: auto; font-feature-settings: normal; font-variation-settings: normal; font-variant-position: normal; font-stretch: normal; font-size: 12px; line-height: normal;"></span>another way to represent netmask addresses called Classless Inter-Domain Routing (CIDR) notation. shown with a slash between the network address and the CIDR value. Thus, the network 192.168.1.0 and netmask 255.255.255.0 would have the CIDR notation of 192.168.1.0/24.

- <span class="s1" style="font-variant-numeric: normal; font-variant-east-asian: normal; font-variant-alternates: normal; font-kerning: auto; font-optical-sizing: auto; font-feature-settings: normal; font-variation-settings: normal; font-variant-position: normal; font-stretch: normal; font-size: 12px; line-height: normal;"></span>Default router (Default gateway):<span class="Apple-converted-space"> </span> With IP and IPv6, devices can communicate directly only with other devices on the same physical network. To connect different physical networks together, you use a router. A router passes data from one private network to another. Usually a network will contain a single router to forward packets to an upper-level network.
- <span class="s1" style="font-variant-numeric: normal; font-variant-east-asian: normal; font-variant-alternates: normal; font-kerning: auto; font-optical-sizing: auto; font-feature-settings: normal; font-variation-settings: normal; font-variant-position: normal; font-stretch: normal; font-size: 12px; line-height: normal;"></span>Hostname: Domain Name System (DNS) assigns a name to IP hosts on the network. each network address is assigned a domain name (such as linux.org) that uniquely identifies the network, and each host in that network is assigned a unique host name, which is added to the domain name to uniquely identify the host on the network. The DNS system uses servers to map host and domain names to the specific network addresses required to communicate with that server. Servers responsible for defining the network and host names for a local network interoperate with upper level DNS servers to resolve remote host names.

- <span class="s1" style="font-variant-numeric: normal; font-variant-east-asian: normal; font-variant-alternates: normal; font-kerning: auto; font-optical-sizing: auto; font-feature-settings: normal; font-variation-settings: normal; font-variant-position: normal; font-stretch: normal; font-size: 12px; line-height: normal;"></span>For a device to communicate in an IP network, it must know three separate pieces of information:

- <span class="s1" style="font-variant-numeric: normal; font-variant-east-asian: normal; font-variant-alternates: normal; font-kerning: auto; font-optical-sizing: auto; font-feature-settings: normal; font-variation-settings: normal; font-variant-position: normal; font-stretch: normal; font-size: 12px; line-height: normal;"></span>Its own host address on the network. Host address: 192.168.20.5
- <span class="s1" style="font-variant-numeric: normal; font-variant-east-asian: normal; font-variant-alternates: normal; font-kerning: auto; font-optical-sizing: auto; font-feature-settings: normal; font-variation-settings: normal; font-variant-position: normal; font-stretch: normal; font-size: 12px; line-height: normal;"></span>The netmask address for the local physical network. Netmask address: 255.255.255.0
- <span class="s1" style="font-variant-numeric: normal; font-variant-east-asian: normal; font-variant-alternates: normal; font-kerning: auto; font-optical-sizing: auto; font-feature-settings: normal; font-variation-settings: normal; font-variant-position: normal; font-stretch: normal; font-size: 12px; line-height: normal;"></span>he address of a local router used to send packets to remote networks. Default gateway: 192.168.20.1

- <span class="s1" style="font-variant-numeric: normal; font-variant-east-asian: normal; font-variant-alternates: normal; font-kerning: auto; font-optical-sizing: auto; font-feature-settings: normal; font-variation-settings: normal; font-variant-position: normal; font-stretch: normal; font-size: 12px; line-height: normal;"></span>IPv6 Address: uses 128-bit addresses instead of the 32-bit addresses. uses hexadecimal numbers. The 128-bit address is split into eight groups of four hexadecimal digits separated by colons, such as : fed1:0000:0000:08d3:1319:8a2e:0370:7334

- <span class="s1" style="font-variant-numeric: normal; font-variant-east-asian: normal; font-variant-alternates: normal; font-kerning: auto; font-optical-sizing: auto; font-feature-settings: normal; font-variation-settings: normal; font-variant-position: normal; font-stretch: normal; font-size: 12px; line-height: normal;"></span>If one or more groups of four digits is 0000, that group or those groups may be omitted, leaving two colons.

- <span class="s1" style="font-variant-numeric: normal; font-variant-east-asian: normal; font-variant-alternates: normal; font-kerning: auto; font-optical-sizing: auto; font-feature-settings: normal; font-variation-settings: normal; font-variant-position: normal; font-stretch: normal; font-size: 12px; line-height: normal;"></span>IPv6 protocol also provides for two different types of host addresses:

- <span class="s1" style="font-variant-numeric: normal; font-variant-east-asian: normal; font-variant-alternates: normal; font-kerning: auto; font-optical-sizing: auto; font-feature-settings: normal; font-variation-settings: normal; font-variant-position: normal; font-stretch: normal; font-size: 12px; line-height: normal;"></span>Link local addresses: on a host device automatically assigns the link local address. The link local address uses a default network address of fe80::and then derives the host part of the address from the media access control (MAC) address built into the network card. This ensures that any IPv6 device can automatically communicate with any other IPv6 device on a local network without any configuration.
- <span class="s1" style="font-variant-numeric: normal; font-variant-east-asian: normal; font-variant-alternates: normal; font-kerning: auto; font-optical-sizing: auto; font-feature-settings: normal; font-variation-settings: normal; font-variant-position: normal; font-stretch: normal; font-size: 12px; line-height: normal;"></span>Global addresses: each network is assigned a unique network address, and each host on the network must have a unique host address.

- <span class="s1" style="font-variant-numeric: normal; font-variant-east-asian: normal; font-variant-alternates: normal; font-kerning: auto; font-optical-sizing: auto; font-feature-settings: normal; font-variation-settings: normal; font-variant-position: normal; font-stretch: normal; font-size: 12px; line-height: normal;"></span>Specific subnetwork ranges are reserved for private IP networks. These private IP addresses can’t be used for Internet traffic; they work only on locac networks.

- <span class="s1" style="font-variant-numeric: normal; font-variant-east-asian: normal; font-variant-alternates: normal; font-kerning: auto; font-optical-sizing: auto; font-feature-settings: normal; font-variation-settings: normal; font-variant-position: normal; font-stretch: normal; font-size: 12px; line-height: normal;"></span>10.0.0.0 to 10.255.255.255
- <span class="s1" style="font-variant-numeric: normal; font-variant-east-asian: normal; font-variant-alternates: normal; font-kerning: auto; font-optical-sizing: auto; font-feature-settings: normal; font-variation-settings: normal; font-variant-position: normal; font-stretch: normal; font-size: 12px; line-height: normal;"></span>172.16.0.0 to 172.31.255.255
- <span class="s1" style="font-variant-numeric: normal; font-variant-east-asian: normal; font-variant-alternates: normal; font-kerning: auto; font-optical-sizing: auto; font-feature-settings: normal; font-variation-settings: normal; font-variant-position: normal; font-stretch: normal; font-size: 12px; line-height: normal;"></span>192.168.0.0 to 192.168.255.255

- <span class="s1" style="font-variant-numeric: normal; font-variant-east-asian: normal; font-variant-alternates: normal; font-kerning: auto; font-optical-sizing: auto; font-feature-settings: normal; font-variation-settings: normal; font-variant-position: normal; font-stretch: normal; font-size: 12px; line-height: normal;"></span>Internet Assigned Numbers Authority (IANA) maintains strict control over the assignment of IP network addresses. it didn’t take long for IANA to run out of available public IP address networks.
- <span class="s1" style="font-variant-numeric: normal; font-variant-east-asian: normal; font-variant-alternates: normal; font-kerning: auto; font-optical-sizing: auto; font-feature-settings: normal; font-variation-settings: normal; font-variant-position: normal; font-stretch: normal; font-size: 12px; line-height: normal;"></span>the idea of network address translation (NAT) saved the day. A NAT server can take an entire private IP network and assign it a single public IP address on the Internet. This is how you can connect your entire home network to a single ISP Internet connection and everything works.

- <span class="s1" style="font-variant-numeric: normal; font-variant-east-asian: normal; font-variant-alternates: normal; font-kerning: auto; font-optical-sizing: auto; font-feature-settings: normal; font-variation-settings: normal; font-variant-position: normal; font-stretch: normal; font-size: 12px; line-height: normal;"></span>The Dynamic Host Configuration Protocol (DHCP): Trying to keep track of host addresses for all of the devices on a large network can become cumbersome.

- <span class="s1" style="font-variant-numeric: normal; font-variant-east-asian: normal; font-variant-alternates: normal; font-kerning: auto; font-optical-sizing: auto; font-feature-settings: normal; font-variation-settings: normal; font-variant-position: normal; font-stretch: normal; font-size: 12px; line-height: normal;"></span>With DHCP, the client communicates with a DHCP server on the network using a temporary address.
- <span class="s1" style="font-variant-numeric: normal; font-variant-east-asian: normal; font-variant-alternates: normal; font-kerning: auto; font-optical-sizing: auto; font-feature-settings: normal; font-variation-settings: normal; font-variant-position: normal; font-stretch: normal; font-size: 12px; line-height: normal;"></span>The DHCP server then tells the client exactly which IP address, netmask address, default gateway, and even DNS server to use.
- <span class="s1" style="font-variant-numeric: normal; font-variant-east-asian: normal; font-variant-alternates: normal; font-kerning: auto; font-optical-sizing: auto; font-feature-settings: normal; font-variation-settings: normal; font-variant-position: normal; font-stretch: normal; font-size: 12px; line-height: normal;"></span>Each time the client reboots, it may receive a different IP address, but that doesn’t matter as long as it’s unique on the network.

- <span class="s1" style="font-variant-numeric: normal; font-variant-east-asian: normal; font-variant-alternates: normal; font-kerning: auto; font-optical-sizing: auto; font-feature-settings: normal; font-variation-settings: normal; font-variant-position: normal; font-stretch: normal; font-size: 12px; line-height: normal;"></span>Servers need to have a fixed IP address so that clients can always find them. While it’s possible to configure static IP addresses in DHCP, usually it’s safest to manually configure the network information for servers. This is called a static host address.

1.  Transport layer: Whereas the network layer helps get data to a specific host on the network, the transport layer helps get the data to the correct application contained on the host. It does that by using ports.

- <span class="s1" style="font-variant-numeric: normal; font-variant-east-asian: normal; font-variant-alternates: normal; font-kerning: auto; font-optical-sizing: auto; font-feature-settings: normal; font-variation-settings: normal; font-variant-position: normal; font-stretch: normal; font-size: 12px; line-height: normal;"></span>Three common transport protocols are used in the IP networking world:

- <span class="s1" style="font-variant-numeric: normal; font-variant-east-asian: normal; font-variant-alternates: normal; font-kerning: auto; font-optical-sizing: auto; font-feature-settings: normal; font-variation-settings: normal; font-variant-position: normal; font-stretch: normal; font-size: 12px; line-height: normal;"></span>Transmission Control Protocol (TCP): transport protocol sends data using a guaranteed delivery method. ensures that the server receives each portion of data that the client computer sends, and vice versa. The downside is that a lot of overhead is required to track and verify all of the data sent, which can slow down the data transfer speed.
- <span class="s1" style="font-variant-numeric: normal; font-variant-east-asian: normal; font-variant-alternates: normal; font-kerning: auto; font-optical-sizing: auto; font-feature-settings: normal; font-variation-settings: normal; font-variant-position: normal; font-stretch: normal; font-size: 12px; line-height: normal;"></span>User Datagram Protocol (UDP): data that’s sensitive to transfer speed (such as real-time data like voice and video), that can cause unwanted delays.
- <span class="s1" style="font-variant-numeric: normal; font-variant-east-asian: normal; font-variant-alternates: normal; font-kerning: auto; font-optical-sizing: auto; font-feature-settings: normal; font-variation-settings: normal; font-variant-position: normal; font-stretch: normal; font-size: 12px; line-height: normal;"></span>Internet Control Message Protocol (ICMP): not used for sending application data. provides a simple way for network devices to pass information such as error messages and network routing information to make it easy for each client to find the required resource on the network.

1.  Application Layer: Where all the action happens. where the network programs process the data sent across the network and then return a result. Most network applications behave using the client/server paradigm. one network device acts as the server, offering some type of service to multiple network clients (such as a web server offering content via web pages). The server listens for incoming connections on a specific transport layer port assigned to the application. The clients must know what transport layer port to use to send requests to the server application. To simplify that process, both TCP and UDP use well-known reserved ports to represent common applications.

Configuring Network

- <span class="s1" style="font-variant-numeric: normal; font-variant-east-asian: normal; font-variant-alternates: normal; font-kerning: auto; font-optical-sizing: auto; font-feature-settings: normal; font-variation-settings: normal; font-variant-position: normal; font-stretch: normal; font-size: 12px; line-height: normal;"></span>systemd-networkd: Linux systems that utilize the systemd initialization method normally use this daemon to detect network interfaces and automatically create entries for them in the network configuration files.
- <span class="s1" style="font-variant-numeric: normal; font-variant-east-asian: normal; font-variant-alternates: normal; font-kerning: auto; font-optical-sizing: auto; font-feature-settings: normal; font-variation-settings: normal; font-variant-position: normal; font-stretch: normal; font-size: 12px; line-height: normal;"></span>no single standard configuration file exists that all distributions use.

- <span class="s1" style="font-variant-numeric: normal; font-variant-east-asian: normal; font-variant-alternates: normal; font-kerning: auto; font-optical-sizing: auto; font-feature-settings: normal; font-variation-settings: normal; font-variant-position: normal; font-stretch: normal; font-size: 12px; line-height: normal;"></span>Debian-based: /etc/network/interfaces file
- <span class="s1" style="font-variant-numeric: normal; font-variant-east-asian: normal; font-variant-alternates: normal; font-kerning: auto; font-optical-sizing: auto; font-feature-settings: normal; font-variation-settings: normal; font-variant-position: normal; font-stretch: normal; font-size: 12px; line-height: normal;"></span>Red Hat–based: /etc/sysconfig/network-scripts directory
- <span class="s1" style="font-variant-numeric: normal; font-variant-east-asian: normal; font-variant-alternates: normal; font-kerning: auto; font-optical-sizing: auto; font-feature-settings: normal; font-variation-settings: normal; font-variant-position: normal; font-stretch: normal; font-size: 12px; line-height: normal;"></span>OpenSUSE: /etc/sysconfig/network file

- <span class="s1" style="font-variant-numeric: normal; font-variant-east-asian: normal; font-variant-alternates: normal; font-kerning: auto; font-optical-sizing: auto; font-feature-settings: normal; font-variation-settings: normal; font-variant-position: normal; font-stretch: normal; font-size: 12px; line-height: normal;"></span>You need to define a DNS server so that the system can use DNS host names.
- <span class="s1" style="font-variant-numeric: normal; font-variant-east-asian: normal; font-variant-alternates: normal; font-kerning: auto; font-optical-sizing: auto; font-feature-settings: normal; font-variation-settings: normal; font-variant-position: normal; font-stretch: normal; font-size: 12px; line-height: normal;"></span>For systemd systems, the DNS server is generated by the systemd-resolved program.
- <span class="s1" style="font-variant-numeric: normal; font-variant-east-asian: normal; font-variant-alternates: normal; font-kerning: auto; font-optical-sizing: auto; font-feature-settings: normal; font-variation-settings: normal; font-variant-position: normal; font-stretch: normal; font-size: 12px; line-height: normal;"></span>For legacy SysVinitsystems, that’s handled in the /etc/resolv.confconfiguration file:

- <span class="s1" style="font-variant-numeric: normal; font-variant-east-asian: normal; font-variant-alternates: normal; font-kerning: auto; font-optical-sizing: auto; font-feature-settings: normal; font-variation-settings: normal; font-variant-position: normal; font-stretch: normal; font-size: 12px; line-height: normal;"></span>domain [mydomain.com](http://mydomain.com) —> defines the domain name assigned to the network. By default, the system will append this domain name to any host names you specify
- <span class="s1" style="font-variant-numeric: normal; font-variant-east-asian: normal; font-variant-alternates: normal; font-kerning: auto; font-optical-sizing: auto; font-feature-settings: normal; font-variation-settings: normal; font-variant-position: normal; font-stretch: normal; font-size: 12px; line-height: normal;"></span>search [mytest.com](http://mytest.com) —> defines any additional domains used to search for host names.
- <span class="s1" style="font-variant-numeric: normal; font-variant-east-asian: normal; font-variant-alternates: normal; font-kerning: auto; font-optical-sizing: auto; font-feature-settings: normal; font-variation-settings: normal; font-variant-position: normal; font-stretch: normal; font-size: 12px; line-height: normal;"></span>nameserver 192.168.1.1 —> where you specify the DNS server assigned to your network.

- <span class="s1" style="font-variant-numeric: normal; font-variant-east-asian: normal; font-variant-alternates: normal; font-kerning: auto; font-optical-sizing: auto; font-feature-settings: normal; font-variation-settings: normal; font-variant-position: normal; font-stretch: normal; font-size: 12px; line-height: normal;"></span>Some networks can have more than one DNS server, just add multiple nameserver entries in the file.

- <span class="s1" style="font-variant-numeric: normal; font-variant-east-asian: normal; font-variant-alternates: normal; font-kerning: auto; font-optical-sizing: auto; font-feature-settings: normal; font-variation-settings: normal; font-variant-position: normal; font-stretch: normal; font-size: 12px; line-height: normal;"></span>Linux command-line tools to set the network configuration information:<span class="Apple-converted-space"> </span>

- <span class="s1" style="font-variant-numeric: normal; font-variant-east-asian: normal; font-variant-alternates: normal; font-kerning: auto; font-optical-sizing: auto; font-feature-settings: normal; font-variation-settings: normal; font-variant-position: normal; font-stretch: normal; font-size: 12px; line-height: normal;"></span>$ nmtui —> Provides a simple text-based menu tool
- <span class="s1" style="font-variant-numeric: normal; font-variant-east-asian: normal; font-variant-alternates: normal; font-kerning: auto; font-optical-sizing: auto; font-feature-settings: normal; font-variation-settings: normal; font-variant-position: normal; font-stretch: normal; font-size: 12px; line-height: normal;"></span>$ nmcli —> Provides a text-only command-line tool

- <span class="s1" style="font-variant-numeric: normal; font-variant-east-asian: normal; font-variant-alternates: normal; font-kerning: auto; font-optical-sizing: auto; font-feature-settings: normal; font-variation-settings: normal; font-variant-position: normal; font-stretch: normal; font-size: 12px; line-height: normal;"></span>Legacy tools (utilities from the net-tools package)

- <span class="s1" style="font-variant-numeric: normal; font-variant-east-asian: normal; font-variant-alternates: normal; font-kerning: auto; font-optical-sizing: auto; font-feature-settings: normal; font-variation-settings: normal; font-variant-position: normal; font-stretch: normal; font-size: 12px; line-height: normal;"></span>$ ethtool —> Displays Ethernet settings for a network interface
- <span class="s1" style="font-variant-numeric: normal; font-variant-east-asian: normal; font-variant-alternates: normal; font-kerning: auto; font-optical-sizing: auto; font-feature-settings: normal; font-variation-settings: normal; font-variant-position: normal; font-stretch: normal; font-size: 12px; line-height: normal;"></span>$ ifconfig —> Displays or sets the IP address and netmask values for a network interface
- <span class="s1" style="font-variant-numeric: normal; font-variant-east-asian: normal; font-variant-alternates: normal; font-kerning: auto; font-optical-sizing: auto; font-feature-settings: normal; font-variation-settings: normal; font-variant-position: normal; font-stretch: normal; font-size: 12px; line-height: normal;"></span>$ iwconfig —> Sets the SSID and encryption key for a wireless interface
- <span class="s1" style="font-variant-numeric: normal; font-variant-east-asian: normal; font-variant-alternates: normal; font-kerning: auto; font-optical-sizing: auto; font-feature-settings: normal; font-variation-settings: normal; font-variant-position: normal; font-stretch: normal; font-size: 12px; line-height: normal;"></span>$ route —> Sets the default router address

- <span class="s1" style="font-variant-numeric: normal; font-variant-east-asian: normal; font-variant-alternates: normal; font-kerning: auto; font-optical-sizing: auto; font-feature-settings: normal; font-variation-settings: normal; font-variant-position: normal; font-stretch: normal; font-size: 12px; line-height: normal;"></span>$ ip (iproute2 Package) —> show / manipulate routing, network devices, interfaces and tunnels
- <span class="s1" style="font-variant-numeric: normal; font-variant-east-asian: normal; font-variant-alternates: normal; font-kerning: auto; font-optical-sizing: auto; font-feature-settings: normal; font-variation-settings: normal; font-variant-position: normal; font-stretch: normal; font-size: 12px; line-height: normal;"></span>/etc/sysctl.conf —> tune networking parameters for a network interface.<span class="Apple-converted-space"> </span> the Linux system uses when interacting with the network interface. such as to disable responding to ICMP messages by setting the icmp_echo_ignore_broadcasts value to 1, or if your system has multiple network interface cards, to disable packet forwarding by setting the ip_forward value to 0

- <span class="s1" style="font-variant-numeric: normal; font-variant-east-asian: normal; font-variant-alternates: normal; font-kerning: auto; font-optical-sizing: auto; font-feature-settings: normal; font-variation-settings: normal; font-variant-position: normal; font-stretch: normal; font-size: 12px; line-height: normal;"></span>Three common DHCP programs are available for Linux systems:

- <span class="s1" style="font-variant-numeric: normal; font-variant-east-asian: normal; font-variant-alternates: normal; font-kerning: auto; font-optical-sizing: auto; font-feature-settings: normal; font-variation-settings: normal; font-variant-position: normal; font-stretch: normal; font-size: 12px; line-height: normal;"></span>dhcpcd
- <span class="s1" style="font-variant-numeric: normal; font-variant-east-asian: normal; font-variant-alternates: normal; font-kerning: auto; font-optical-sizing: auto; font-feature-settings: normal; font-variation-settings: normal; font-variant-position: normal; font-stretch: normal; font-size: 12px; line-height: normal;"></span>dhclient
- <span class="s1" style="font-variant-numeric: normal; font-variant-east-asian: normal; font-variant-alternates: normal; font-kerning: auto; font-optical-sizing: auto; font-feature-settings: normal; font-variation-settings: normal; font-variant-position: normal; font-stretch: normal; font-size: 12px; line-height: normal;"></span>pump

- <span class="s1" style="font-variant-numeric: normal; font-variant-east-asian: normal; font-variant-alternates: normal; font-kerning: auto; font-optical-sizing: auto; font-feature-settings: normal; font-variation-settings: normal; font-variant-position: normal; font-stretch: normal; font-size: 12px; line-height: normal;"></span>Bonding allows you to aggregate multiple interfaces into one virtual network device.

- <span class="s1" style="font-variant-numeric: normal; font-variant-east-asian: normal; font-variant-alternates: normal; font-kerning: auto; font-optical-sizing: auto; font-feature-settings: normal; font-variation-settings: normal; font-variant-position: normal; font-stretch: normal; font-size: 12px; line-height: normal;"></span>Load balancing: Network traffic is shared between two or more network interfaces.
- <span class="s1" style="font-variant-numeric: normal; font-variant-east-asian: normal; font-variant-alternates: normal; font-kerning: auto; font-optical-sizing: auto; font-feature-settings: normal; font-variation-settings: normal; font-variant-position: normal; font-stretch: normal; font-size: 12px; line-height: normal;"></span>Aggregation: Two or more network interfaces are combined to create one larger network pipe.
- <span class="s1" style="font-variant-numeric: normal; font-variant-east-asian: normal; font-variant-alternates: normal; font-kerning: auto; font-optical-sizing: auto; font-feature-settings: normal; font-variation-settings: normal; font-variant-position: normal; font-stretch: normal; font-size: 12px; line-height: normal;"></span>Active/passive: One network interface is live, and the other is used as a backup for fault tolerance.
